SEPERATING MAN FROM NATURE?

•

Do you want to live in a synthetic biosphere domesticated for human
use?

•

Can we create a synthetic biosphere, and integrate GMO animals and
plants into all aspects of our lives?

•

Universal Veganism?

We can use urban terraforming on Earth to separate people from nature and let it
flourish independently from human existence. We will create technology to create a
purely synthetic biosphere that people can replicate and live in readily, that will fulfill us.
On Earth, we can move people and all our farming into cities, in a similar way to life on a
space station. Cloning and genetic manipulation is great for domesticating things for
human beings, so long as we don’t use that technology on humans. Humans and nature
are not things to use in of themselves. We can eventually do genetic experimentation
and gene editing in large super computer simulations, and print out plants or animals
from them. Turning biology into a pure software problem is essential to going to the
stars, so that we can broadcast a planets genome and structure, to the universe, in
whatever way we see fit.

Creating synthetic meat, synthetic organs, could be all very useful. Printing a lung or
heart for transplant, is in the near future. These are possible good uses, though it is a
very careful line to walk between being useful and being ultimately toxic. Printing meat
for consumption, may be the way we eat meat in the future, tuned to perfect taste,
texture, and nutrition. We might just have tasty healthy GMO animals/fish/bugs we feed
and eat. It is unknowable. Any solution though will maximize health, efficiency, and
ethics. Killing animals may become completely unacceptable, for the ethics of respecting

all life with brains. Killing plants will probably always be ok, so long as they are grown
for human use, and not harvested from nature. We may one day make cutting down a
forest a crime, while trees we grow for specific uses, will be ok to cut down. That ethical
line in food is being battled and tested out in the developed world today: veganism,
vegetarianism, pescetarianism, minimal meat eaters, organic, sustainable, fair trade.
Ideology will give way to reality eventually. What is that line for you?

CHAPTER 2: APPLIED ERTHICS IN CAPITALISM

Human beings like companies that are human oriented, do amazing things, and
make their human lives better.

We need to focus on the world we live in to build the future, and not predict the future.
We can use thought experiments on what we need as a galactic civilization to inspire
what we do now. My thought experiments are not descriptions of the future, I want to
exist, they are questions about the kind of future we can create, and our ethical role and
connection to that. They can be judged by how much useful innovation they inspire in
the immediate present.

MODERN TECH HISTORY AND OUR HUMANITY

STANDARD OIL:

The oil industry gave us all the technological progress we see today. It was oil alone that
created the modern world, and all the wealth and amazing technology we have. Coal
made the industrial revolution happen, oil took that to whole other level. We can look at
Standard Oil, from our time and just see a big evil oil monopoly. From the perspective of
the people that first used Standard Oils products, they experienced something far more
intimately human and more transformative than when people first got personal
computers. Standard Oil, brought cheap and safe lamp oil into people’s homes, and lite
the streets of dark cities. Common people could stay up and read. The very first night
owls without ancestral estates, could be born. This company brought light to an age and
became one of the first great technology companies of history, that ushered in the

greatest age of human progress and development that had ever been experienced for
mankind.

Standard oil didn’t drill for oil, they standardized it and shipped it. They created the
network for it to reach people in the cheapest and most efficient way. Railroads where
the new technology, and standard oil used railways smarter and better than anyone
before. They integrated and used the highest-level technology of the time, to deliver the
most valuable product possible for the enhancement of human life. Books existed, rails
existed, lighting existed, the telegraph existed, printing presses existed. Cheap light
integrated them all. If standard oil had maintained a focus on the betterment of
humanity and expanding human expression and experience, they may not have been
burned at the stake as an evil witch at the turn of the century. People did not feel this
company was out for them, and latched onto fear mongering and yellow journalism, that
amplified their fears, and justified the eventual break up of this company. The fault lies
in the company, and its inability to grasp the deeper morality of technology that we
must embrace. The downfall of Standard Oil is a great American tragedy that should
never be celebrated as a victory for mankind. There was no such thing as Robber
Barons. Americas killing of great tech tycoons, only made growth and development
slower.

COROLLARY STORIES: BELL

The story of Bell Communications is not much different. They made great tech, changed
human life, connected people across great distances, changed human life for the better,
got lost in their own power, became something people feared, and got broken up. Great
tech companies that stop innovating, and focus on expansion and domination, become
unpopular fast. Now as great tech companies arise again our fears rise up, and when

lies, scandals and yellow journalism make a perfect storm, many of the great companies
will be smashed. We smashed down Microsoft in the 1990’s, because it was a very
inhumane tech company, that most people hated, and was focused only on its own
market share and power. Beneath that though is certainly damage to the industry and
free enterprise, that we will never see in the things not created. The pretend idealistic
faces tech companies put on is an act to stop them from being smashed and broken up
by the people. Capitalism is learning to have a fake human face at all levels.

19 T H CENTURY INTERNET AND KODAK

Internet technology has been around since the American civil war; we just
didn’t have the vision to really use to its fullest.

Telegraph wires, cheap newspaper printing, typewriters, and good lighting, where the
first internet. Newspapers where the display, and telegraph wires the communication
medium, with reporters being the interface of connection between the machines and the
masses. Typewriters expanded people’s capacity to write and communicate to a much
broader audience. They could extend users thoughts out with typing machines.
Tickertape machines, could print out messages sent over a telegraph wire. While it
would have been ridiculously expensive, we could imagine a primitive SMS like text
messaging system working between homes. We could have invented a communication
system between people’s homes, that would have allowed them to message others via
telegraph wires, before the invention of the phone. The tech existed in the 1870’s.

If we understood in the past the fundamental value in communication to our humanity,
and the power and dignity existing in all human beings, we could have directed

technological development better, and more towards the very things we have today. This
is not about government policy, or religion. It is about really committing to humanity,
taking risks, and focusing on humanity. Great companies wouldn’t have fallen if they had
been more like this. The risk inherent in experimentation can be greatly mitigated by a
focus on humanity. All great tech aligns with being more human, and thus we can have
direction in time and space to direct development, even if we don’t know what we will
develop.

Kodak invented digital cameras and didn’t use them, because their profits were based in
film sales. Digital cameras meant no film to sell, thus no value to Kodak’s bottom line.
Kodak lost focus on creating real value for the customers and their humanity, and used
people as tools to fill their coffers. Kodak died. Most tech companies die, and much of
the great tech they discover doesn’t get made at the earliest stages possible. HP makes
printer cartridges that are overpriced and deep down useless, to make money, and failed
as a tech company. It once stood at the pinnacle of respect for humanity.

APPLE

Steve made great technology over and over again because he had a proper orientation
in time, an understanding of what technology really was, and the way to connect it to
human beings. Steve Jobs described the first Mac as a bicycle for the mind. Steve Jobs
brought mankind into a tighter man to machine symbiosis that rewards our humanity
and feels fundamentally human in our lives. Apple is a great cybernetics company.
Apples future lies in its ability to connect more of our lives into technology all around us.
As a brand, Apple has to make products that connect the highest-level technology, with
ease of use, and a fundamental enhancement of our humanity.

So how can Apple make technology to push us closer to the stars and more
deeply into the humanity of we are, as a leading cybernetics company?

I don’t see much going for them, unless they seriously change course. They are in a
corporate death spiral like the companies before them, and will focus on making profits
as they do now, and will not undermine that profit stream to make a truly great new
product. The Apple tech stack is chasing subscription money, with zero innovation over
the competition. It has no service to humanity, the future, or our deeper connection to
technology.

Airpods and Apple watches, form a backbone for a new cybernetics interface other than
touch screens on a phone, that tries to tackle the problem of zombie like staring into
people’s phones, connecting people to the world more, and using AI integrated into daily
life. They have some hope there. Their overall platform with a new vision can again step
out and change the world. How to beat zombies is Apples great challenge for humanity,
that they can and should solve. It is doable.

TRANSPORTATION EVOLVED:

Technology exists to make us more human.
I never dreamt of flying in the clouds. In my vivid dreams, I hovered a few feet above
the surface of the earth skipping and skimming across large distances. Tech that can do
this, would make me as happiest as possible. Our literal dreams of how we can travel,

can be the reality of how we make future transportation. If you really want to make
people more human, they need to run, swim, jump, or even fly!

A person moving between two reasonable near locations, needs a system of
transportations that makes them more human, more alive. Driverless cars will
revolutionize logistics, and are not the ideal way we move as people. People using
driverless cars will be little different than iPhone zombies all staring into their phones on
a metro system. A transportation system that makes us fatter, disconnected, and lazier,
is coming in our near future. We can do better than this by thinking more deeply on
what we want as human beings, other than cheaper, faster, more convenient
transportation between two points.

Bicycles may seem like an ideal system: healthy, open, social, connected. Motorists hate
bicyclists because they slow down transportation for everyone, makes driving much
more complex, and the road becomes more about the cyclists’ feelings than actually
going places the fastest you can. Most people don’t want to go on bicycles because they
are slow, make you look poor, and not all that safe. Electric motors make them more
ethical, faster, and pragmatic. You can get places more efficiently, at more entertaining
speeds, while not hindering efficient flow of traffic. Repetitive and healthy pedaling on
electric bicycles is not as human as we can make transportation. Motorcycles are the
most human feeling, and the most unsafe form of travel. Cool electric bikes that don’t
make you look poor, have some potential.

Exoskeletons that can allow us to run at over 40 km/h would be far closer to what we
ultimately want. We could run and jump to work. The system could teach you how to use
your body, and how to do amazing things with it. Normal people could do parkour like
stunts, with the help of exoskeletons. You could even turn on a training mode, where

moving becomes even harder than in real life so that you can develop yourself, and
possibly charge the battery. A system that trains and develops our bodies into the
absolutely best form they can be in, while empowering us to run around like super
heroes, would be far more fun for me then any car. We could step out of those
machines, and have even more powerful, healthy, and beautiful bodies, capable of doing
amazing things without them. We could literally wear an “iPhone” as clothes. Where
Apple becomes more than just a bicycle for your mind, it becomes one for your body
too.

The basic suit wouldn’t even need motors or balancing machines. It would just a frame
that fits most comfortably over your body that can create natural resistance for every
single muscle group as you move, and not restrict your ability to work in confined spaces
close to people. The connection to the body and its ability to move around with other
people, would be more central to design, than enhancements to a person. It becomes far
easier to develop something that people could use in their lives, when it isn’t about being
super strong or fast. It could be used on earth as a training machine for people to get
the strongest, healthiest bodies, with the least risk when working out. Rather than
having a power suit that makes things easier, it makes things harder in order to keep
your body healthy. This is far easier to develop than more complex robotic machines.
Robot development, and creating a physical interface for the body to inhabit in, are 2
very different kinds of research and development.

The resistance and training aspects of an exoskeleton are the humanity in the machine
that will make it more useful and guide it towards faster development. The humanity and
not the power are the thing that makes it practical, and drives its development. Such a
device would be essential for those living in low gravity environments in space.
Developing the device with space in mind, will launch the product forward faster and

with deeper insights into its grander purposes and uses. I envision future with people
that have nearly perfect and fit bodies from constant physical training and activity, and
massive space stations being like parkour wonderlands. The way to make life more fun,
is to make us more alive and human. A body training exoskeleton can be developed now
at vastly lower costs, and have immediate value for many people.

MY IDEAL “BICYCLE”: THE FAILURE OF SEGWAY SCOOTERS

A Segway scooter is a rather cool but inhuman technology. It replaces walking with a
machine. From its very first day, it seemed a toy for a very fat person, that leads to a
Wall-E like world. The technology can be made more human and not replace exercise.
Segway like technology has evolved into mono-wheel devices, where you step on each
side of a single wheel that self-balances, and you fly around a city freer than on a
traditional Segway. The tech had to evolve to be more human or die. The change though
didn’t come from within the company, another company made it more human, got sued
by Segway, and then Segway got bought by them.

A self-balancing Segway mono-wheel (Segway One S1) is a cool technology, and can be
made even more human. It is a great direction for a technology and in of itself a great
product for many young people to buy. It can get people around a city quickly, be
carried and charged anywhere easily, and go easily into one’s home. It isn’t suitable for
people that can’t afford to fall down often, and like feeling safe. What we need is a
device that has more structure, that can still go on subways, elevators, and into homes
easily, while being fun and free, and can make people more physically fit using it. It is

combining the mono-wheels advantages with an electric bikes advantages, and not their
uncool drawbacks.

A combination of a Segway One S1 with a “HalfBike” (http://halfbikes.com/ ), is like a
Segway with one wheel, that you can peddle on standing up, with handlebars. You take
a half bike use a large One S1 for a main wheel, and don’t use 2 small back wheels. You
would lean forward to go faster, and lean back to go slower, with breaks and
acceleration augmenting and assisting the alignment of the rider. It would feel like
superman flying over the surface of the road. This can become consumer technology we
could have today. It can even be used as a powered push cart to carry heavy things as
you walk around a city and take public transportation. This could empower people of any
age, with its multiple purposes.

The exact way to make this, I don’t know, and I am not even sure this is the right way.
Maybe we need to do the same idea, but with a cool recumbent bike that you sit back
into, and that has a seat frame that creates some roll bars around you. Being seated like
a Formula 1 driver would be the ideal position for a bike you sit back into. It just seems
clear that self-balancing wheels can make for a single wheel bicycle that will be much
easier to move around in the world and use.

CYBORGS AND ANDROIDS

We don’t have to cut off any body parts to become cyborgs. Machines can encase our
bodies and minds and enhance existing systems, and make them healthier. Androids are
not a technology we ever need. If we can build a human like android body we can build
ideal exoskeletons, that encase the body. Science Fiction androids and traditional

cyborgs are emotional stories that explore what it is to be human and not about what we
should actually build. There is something innately more human in exoskeletons. We as
human beings will want minimum encasement, maximum enhancement. We will wear
our machines as extensions of ourselves, and look better as we are, with them on, and
not hidden away behind them.

Cyborgs are the degree to which technology takes over our humanity. All cyborgs in SciFi should be seen as stories exploring the line at what point technology makes us more
human, or less human, if we become something greater through the enhancements, or if
the enhancements become our very identity. The stories that better capture the moral
story and the proper vision of the hard tech, are far more compelling. Ironman captured
cybernetics in a more realistic way, in terms of man’s relationship to it. The armor is an
excellent metaphor for the man to machine relationship that our future is heading
towards. The story evolves with him struggling to keep his humanity, with the
overwhelming technological power he possesses around him. He even ends up creating a
nearly perfect android. The story makes a mistake and Vision should be the mental and
physical extension of Tony Stark, manifested in machines, surrounding both his body
and mind. The more “human” Vision becomes, the more human the interface that Tony
can connect into, and not lose his own humanity.

MONETIZING SPACE: SPACEX AND FRIENDS

MY PATH TO MARS:

Space exploration and colonization must be profit and freedom driven. Capitalism must
go to space at every step of the way. The Apollo missions were a failure because they
didn’t primarily focus NASA on making a capitalist commercial space industry. Step one
of making a business in space is getting over NASA and the Apollo project as ideals, and
see them as the problem. They create unrealistic goals, use poor economics, and deny
the underlying reality of the universe. Going to Mars is not the natural next step after
landing on the moon. Building up a massive and profitable low earth orbit space
industry, is the first step. Then we have to find profitable reasons to develop the Moon,
and have people traveling there. Only after this, and with massive resources and
development in space, will any mission to mars really be conceivable.

Mass monetization of low earth orbit is being done by SpaceX and other companies at a
tremendous pace, after the US government allowed more economic freedom for
capitalism to do so. It will be much cheaper to get useful things into orbit, that can
directly benefit life on Earth, that would not have been profitable enough before under a
government run system. Space tourism can soon be a real industry, and hopefully other
things as well, that we haven’t yet imagined. SpaceX wants to go to Mars and their plan
is just not realistic, nor based on how we will really get there in the future. Mars, The
Moon and low earth orbit need to first be colonized by machines at massive scales,
which then will make it possible to bring people into space.

Housing quantum computers that need to run at near absolute zero, could be what
drives the colonization of space. There needs to be something that can drive a high profit
“gold rush” like moment into space, and not just people’s curious feelings. The Moon and
low Earth Orbit could eventually be a giant server base for quantum computers that
need extremely low temperatures to run. The overall colonization of the galaxy might be
driven by finding more resources to build massive computers farms, to support human

industry and life. The large planets in our solar systems only value to future generations
will be in machines turning them into massive computers, running at low temperatures.
We can never land on them as people, nor easily get anything off their surface.

This all begins by building up lots of space stations around the Earth. Space hotels can
gradually develop themselves one iteration after the other to support human life. As we
get better at domesticating space stations and making them suitable for real human
living, then we can create real space craft that can travel between worlds. We can then
turn space stations into cruise ships. They can take short trips to the moon for the
coolest trip of a person’s life. As we get better at this, we will slowly upgrade the craft to
with more safety features, human comforts, and even shields for cosmic radiation. Then
we take remote building and resource harvesting devices, and land them on the moon.
We can create a moon base on the moon, that requires no people to build it. We need to
build up this tech on the earth first, and build whole cities in desolate and remote
locations, with local resources supplying most of the construction materials. Mass robotic
construction is a pre-requisite of space travel.

We then create a series hotels that stay in orbit over the Moon. Cruise ships will then
serve as ferries between the Earth and the Moons space stations. The moon bases first
purpose is a safety net for people on stations in orbit. Stations above the earth, can
readily use escape pods to escape down to the Earth, and will need similar safety options
with the Moon. With hotels in orbit, and primitive living spaces on the surface, we can
get people to the moon at a larger and faster scale, than if straight making a full moon
colony. Advanced cruise ships will take excursions down to the moon, and people will
primarily live in orbit on stations in orbit. Moving between stations and the moon’s
surface doesn’t require that much fuel. The moon base then can work on expanding its

size and supporting services. Producing food, back up air and water, fuel for the station
and rockets, in a gradual step by step process.

The moon will eventually provide a resource and manufacturing base to create space
stations. Getting resources off of its surface will always be vastly simpler than getting
them off of the Earth. By this point in space development, we should have fairly large
amounts of money being made in Space and new ways to commercialize it. Mars probes
will have already been sent, and all the remote building tech used on the Moon, that was
first developed for future cities on the Earth, will go to Mars, and just build. The primitive
universal construction machines won’t need resources from Earth, and can hopefully just
replicate themselves and mass build on Mars. We may need to send large shipments of
electronics to put brains into the machines. By that time, all processors will be made in
space, and most of the worlds computer servers will be based in space.

It will be people in space stations above Mars that colonize mars, and not living in
settlements on Mars that really live “on” that world first. It will be much better to live on
a space station with artificial gravity, than the Mars surface for any extended time.
Systems to live on the surface will have to grow slowly over time, and exist for
emergency, entertainment, and practical business purposes, at first. The driving forces
to make this possible will be for technological money-making ventures that are
independent of those in space, which in turn can finance man’s journey into space.
Space has to be overwhelming profitable and productive compared to each person that
would live off the Earth. Quantum computer cooling is one highly profitable possibility at
this moment, short of the desire for people to be free of government.

THE INHUMANITY OF MARS

Sending people to Mars is evil, and can only be driven by vanity and suicidal impulses. If
someone really believed going to mars would lead man forward into the future, then
they could justify their sacrifice of their life as noble, and for something greater. It is not
the immediate path to the stars and not our near future though. The amount of
infrastructure needed on Mars before even sending people there for more than a “hey I
went to mars, I am famous!!” moment, is very substantial. Mars tourism to feed rich
bored peoples egos, is hardly the foundations of technology. To really solve the space
monetization problem, we need to go back to first principles and not vapid idealism; the
mars journey has to be fundamentally empowering to people and humanity, and not just
a massive PR stunt for being human.

The main focus should be getting people up into space safely and able to stay in safe
reliable space stations in near earth orbit. The stations could be monetized for tourism,
research labs, and even high-end manufacturing. Monetizing space is not sexy, it is
reality. If a business man in 1850, said, I am going to revolutionize the world with train
travel, where you can ship coal from the remote mines of the world, right to grand coal
power plants/furnaces, to power industry, people probably wouldn’t be jumping up in joy
to invest. That though is the reality of trains, they move coal and oil mostly. The
romantic visions of travel, where not what they really did. SpaceX is a train network for
space. Let’s in reality move things that pay the most per load, while selling a sexy image
of travel to the most exotic possible location, like long range trains of old did.

What sort of death rate is acceptable for commercial space travel?

Dreaming of space travel and dying in space are two very different things. A large
disaster with 200 dead tourists could derail the whole commercialization of space. With
people, fully aware of the risks, the absolute hell and possibility of a gruesome death,
and signing every form to acknowledge that, it doesn’t take away from the actual horror
that will come. People don’t see reality until there are actual dead bodies, or they are
lying half dead in a hospital bed. Getting people “into space” will probably be a more
remote thing, with businesses running them from the Earths ground and people “living”
in space via VR.

AR/VR/MR: SNAP INC, FACEBOOK

Video chat is not a popular product now, it is in theory this amazing technology, that few
people actually use, and if they do, only with a small number of people. Having a live
video chat with active face and background filters, is where things are going. They are
now building very basic filters that can do the mechanics, and send little video posts.
This is great in of itself. The issues are in what sort of ideas define those filters, why
people will use them, and the ultimate moral value in their existence. Being able to
make my face into a dog, is cute, and only goes so far. Creating video filters that
enhance humanity and not feed vanity is a challenging task.

EYE CONTACT FILTER:

A very basic filter of moral value and that is cool would to be able to have eye contact
with a person while video chatting with them. When you are looking at someone’s eyes
during a video chat, you are not looking at the camera, which then allows them to see
into your eyes. It is mostly polite on a video chat to stare into the camera half of the

time. If you always look in the camera, then you won’t see the other person and really
connect with them. Video filters will be able to shift your eyes to be looking at someone,
when you are looking at the screen. Simply shifting the pupils to appear to be looking at
you, is just taking an eye and shifting its alignment in an eye socket. This is not fake
emotion or lying. It isn’t a video filter to make you look more beautiful than you are, or
hide you. It doesn’t create a more plastic like reality; it creates a more real and intimate
reality.

AR PRIVACY BACKGROUND FILTER:

If you are in public video chatting, you can make those around you very uncomfortable.
They don’t know if they are on camera and being watched. It just creates an immediate
discomfort in many people. You also may not want others seeing the people in your
environment. Privacy filters can be imbedded into the background. Cameras in general
looking out at the world can have faces or even whole people blurred out, unless they
stare at the camera for like 5 seconds and give a thumbs-up. This will make people
around you far more comfortable to be around people video chatting. People will also be
more comfortable that people around them won’t troll or disrupt their chat as easily.
They have to trust that their privacy can’t be violated without permission, even when
they are being view directly by a camera. Privacy filters on cameras in general will make
people more comfortable with cameras around them, if they know there is inherent
software protecting their privacy.

An AR/MR reality can edit out other people and create a more intimate reality, where
you are connecting with people you want to connect with, rather than an impersonal
world. Humans are tribal and clannish, and yet gain great benefit from living in big cities
and in large populations. We can get the benefits of a small town and big city, at some

emotional level. AR can edit out all the things not connected to us, and focus our
attention on what is important. A more fun aspect would be to “blur” people by
transforming them into other things. Reality itself can be bent into something else.
These transformations don’t have to be random or meaningless. Possibly the person
themselves can set what they are blurred into, and this becomes a sort of social armor
and clothes contained within a AR reality. I personally wouldn’t mind being a mini-T-Rex
Raptor, running around New York City, when cameras spot me and shield my privacy.
When I meet up with other t-rexes we can have street fights with our avatars, and never
physically touch each other. A living combat video game played right in the streets.

You don’t need a centralized system controlling such a thing. When people are seen, info
can be sent from them on how to see them. Cameras themselves have to lose privacy
and collectively we can know what local cameras are pointed in what direction and if
they are seeing us, and we can shape how they see us. We simply make a protocol that
makes all cameras pointed at the world broadcast to a sort of localized internet, the
orientation of the camera and what it can take in. Other systems can determine what is
in that cameras view, rather than the camera itself, and then send back info on what it
should block or alter its image into. We may have to lose the freedom to point cameras
out at the world, without restrictions by others. People will be fearful of cameras they
don’t protect their privacy, and be more accepting of ones not stripping them of their
privacy, and so even without any laws, the natural outcome will be regulated cameras.
Good cameras add value to everything they see in real time, and people become more
empowered by the cameras in the world, that serve individual needs and empower
people beyond the camera owner. Systems that feed into and support a collective socialcommons will be more accepted and integrated into society.

We can’t alter things to cover up our humanity. We alter the reality to enhance our
humanity and to respect others privacy and dignity. There could be a “just got up in the
morning filter” that makes you more beautiful, though we need to enhance other aspects
humanity building elements to compensate. Human vanity can’t be the basis of such a
technology and it can’t also deny that human vanity can be a driving force in the
development of AR filters that makes us look more desirable, and hide the ugly us. Very
few people make avatars that look uglier than they are in real life. Cameras that look out
at the world, need to not just humanize the person using the camera, but to
fundamentally humanize the people on the camera, and add value into their lives, such
that people will not mind a camera observing them.

3D CARTOON AI ANALYTICS REPRESENTATION

We can use silly video chat face filters to create Emotional intelligence augmentation and
make communicating face to face online, far deeper and more meaningful. Much of the
initial development by companies will be in making us into 3d cartoon version of
ourselves. We will live in a cartoon reality. This will certainly make people too shy to be
on camera, more open to being “seen”. If there aren’t sensors seeing our real face and
translating our emotions in real time into the chat, then it is a lip-syncing toy. It could in
time develop more social value, as the cartoons have valuable social info imbedded in
them. Such as if the app could read the bigger emotional expressions you are emoting,
and in real time create exaggerated them with your animated face, this would have high
value for our humanity and understanding people more.

In a sense the AI, knows you a certain way, and represents that knowledge in cartoon
form in a chat. It can create a more humanizing reality, in a completely cartoon
rendered version of it. Our inner emotionally reality that is perceivable by machine

intelligence could be rendered into an exaggerated visual metaphor, that can allow our
emotions and nature to be seen more deeply by those around us. Common metaphors
and cartoon characters will take on a deeper meaning, and form a collective visual
language. The representations of meaningful information that computers can draw out
about us and show to others, can exist in nearly any form of art and sound. The metacommunications we know now only infer weakly through body language and facial
expressions. Not everyone is equally good at reading these things, and machines
themselves can enhance the sort of emotional intelligence of most people, in much the
same way calculators make everyone better at math.

ORIENTING TO SPACE: COMIC BOOK CHAT!

People on colonies and space stations, need “warm-fuzzies” to hold them through the
nearly unbearable distance and cold. Sixteen minute times between communications,
creates a need for something like video chat without video chat. Sending video
messages infused with humor, art, writing messages on the video, sounds, and voices,
are mostly what we can do now. These are not good for a linear conversation. Going
from video to video, makes it hard to really create a conversation. We can use Mixed
reality images rather than video and have a “comic book” conversation!

You talk into the camera, have your face recorded in video. The app then takes a best
image of you, and renders your voice to text, summarizes, and organizes it, and then
puts it in a comic book style with text bubbles. A 30 second message could be broken up
into 4-8 panels. The images could be real and the best one to match your meaning to
each panel of the comic. Cartoon versions of your face could also be made that highly
exaggerate your emotions in the message. These will all be thematically connected into
an overall story.

Your key points and emotions will be highlighted and possibly summarized so the person
doesn’t miss anything important. Key information or next steps needed to be taken will
be presented. There can be panels of action imbued with the text ones, to create a real
“story”. The app could expand beyond just your face and create images out of what you
say, that connect into an overall clear pattern. If I say I want some coffee, there will be
an image of me wanting coffee represented in some form, with my face. This also can
connect into actual services, and things connecting into the real world. Send a message
of “Hey buddy you need a pizza, a beer and hug” and the person can click on a link that
brings them these things. This would be useful technology on Earth, and create many
business and marketing opportunities.

MAIN THEMES OF NEW CHATTING

Social and moral value in a comic/cartoon reality can be to emphasize emotions and
contexts, that are hard to directly infer for people. It can lead to clearer communication
and help connect people into the real world directly around them more, rather than
purely into a virtualized world. This can also help communication between different
cultures, genders, races. Often people can’t see “Black peoples”-Asians-Whites faces/fat
people’s faces/Ugly peoples value/opposite sex faces and infer
meanings/emotions/hidden contexts, and so on. This all makes for more intense
emotional connections separated by physical and/or cognitive distances. Our emotional
distances from people exist in space, time, and cognition.

OPENHR --TECHNOLOGY AND CORPORATE CULTURE:

My ideal HR platform is an open platform, that maximizes benefit to the employees, and
fundamentally respects and values them, not just as cogs in a corporate machine. What
people really want and need more than a job is a career. HR must be structured around
the careers of people and not a job, set in one company. Workers jobs will become more
fluid, their careers more defined, and get the best deal for their abilities. HR should
serve the workers and not the companies themselves, because people will want to work
more for companies that use such a system, and the companies themselves may get far
higher performance from workers and have the right people for the right job.

Apple, Google, and few others, alone have some fairly developed HR systems. They
should merge all their systems, and create an open tech stack and data set, that other
companies big and small can readily connect into. Create an OpenHR platform that they
all can view and share that allows members to directly recruit people from within other
companies. Only member companies with open data themselves, and matching HR
policies, will be able to view that data. Using such a system will make your company
have a more attractive company culture for future employees, and look better based on
real accountable information. Customers, the government, investors, corporate partners,
and employees, will trust you more

Companies would be able to view and hire people freely. Workers can move between
companies freely, and to be bided on in a more open and free market. The humanity and
abilities of workers need to shine outwards, and so people can be in the right place at
the right time, doing the right project, with the right benefits. If you have good
company, with good projects, and treat people well, then people will want to come work
for you, and work on your projects, to help make your companies vision a reality. If
companies acquire many talented people and they get recruited readily by other
companies, that can be a good thing for your company, because it will allow them to

recruit very talented people easier. There can also be recruitment bonuses paid out to
the company that finds and develops great workers, to compensate for the hassle, and
more motivate them to let workers go. Workers will not just leave a good company
doing work that they believe in, for a slightly higher paycheck. People will want to be on
the projects that match them best. Companies will need to attract and sell their ideas to
their workers.

Being able to hire people from other companies and share workers, can also allow
companies to share knowledge and abilities, allowing technology to integrate across
companies more readily, and for products to develop faster. If I was a good company
and I had former workers, that I still have good relationships with, working in other
companies that I respect, that would certainly be useful and valuable to my company.
Good and talented people, will want to work for companies with an OpenHR system.
They will value the freedom, and dignity that comes with it. They know that they can get
to the career they really want to more easily. Working for a smaller start-up, with lower
pay, can more readily catapult them into higher position at better companies, if that is
what they want.

Companies pessimism, fear, and protecting themselves is stripped away; workers are
put first, so that the best companies can succeed, and people can work in the best
places, in the best projects, for them. This is not idealistic, it is pragmatically realistic
and good way to get great workers, and use them at their best. You know you won’t be
trapped in a dying company, or horrible job, that lured you in with seductive
recruitment, when you start a new job with this high-powered career building HR
system. Companies will need to focus more on the development of their workers by
creating more useful skills and experiences for them, because they workers will want to
do what builds their career.

Data on workers, can be used for their benefit first and not the companies. Workers than
will more directly contribute and be open to sharing their data, because that data, will
power their career. This leads to a higher embracement of training and having their
weakness and flaws exposed. Which in turn leads to better workers, operating a higher
efficiency, which in turn makes them more desirable and hirable by other companies and
into other projects. At the root of this system is a more dynamic, living, AI powered
“resume/CV”, that describes workers value, experience, skills, knowledge, social
networks, and whatever of value. Workers would feel empowered to be shown so clearly
and be recruited from this data, if they know it served them.

Being able to actively track, train, and develop skills, continuously over a career is
essential for workers. The “fake” credentials, certificates, and college degrees’ people
acquire in life to look good, don’t inherently in of themselves denote any actual
functional intelligence or the ability to overcome real adversity. Going to Harvard doesn’t
say as much as people imagine about someone’s actual skills. Companies have to pay
high prices to hire these prestige people with no inherent superior talent.

The system

must overcome the corporatism of hiring inferior people with good credentials, where HR
protects itself by hiring people from top universities that aren’t actually the best people.

At another level, social connections are what people most value from work. These social
connections, relationships and sense of value gained from them, have to be magnified
and rewarded. Most companies hire through the social networks of their staff, when they
can. When companies are posting jobs, they have already failed at some level in the
hiring process. Real HR has to be more about communication and not the high-end
filtering of resumes and hunting talent with AI hunting dogs for headhunters. While I

don’t know how, there must already be tools to empower and track social connections
between staff, far beyond some internal Facebook system.

If companies could come together, share, and integrate all their tech and HR policies,
develop a universal HR for all of them, there could be something up and running rather
quickly. Such a system would be a massive threat to the existing hierarchy of any
system. All the corporate politics could be crushed away, and useless management
rendered obsolete and fired. Large companies at some level don’t like talented workers,
in the way their internal politics and real HR systems work. Talent is a threat to existing
hierarchy because people don’t want to hire people that can replace them. A system that
amplifies talent, will be an existential threat to corporatists in a company. Actual results
and not social games will define business. Careers need to be built with talent.

SPACE:

Space can inspire this HR system. You can’t recruit and hire so easily in space. A mars
colony may have 20 different companies operating different businesses, and they will
need to share workers in order to get things done. There will need to be an overarching
vision and purpose greater than companies’ day to day success. The very world they live
in needs to be made better, and as that world is made better, their industry improves,
and their company profits, if it is aligned with the “greater good”. Making great
technology is a mission! It can build the world, and the future. When we invest in the
future, we will arrive at that future sooner. In space, this reality is life and death.

COMMUNICATION SYSTEMS.

People love to hear what they want to hear. Many people in companies become
very good at telling people what they want to hear, or already believe. This is
how professional liars work.

The essence of good communication is communicating things that are fundamentally for
the good and benefit of the other person, and not just yourself. People really want to
take in and really think about what is empowering and helpful to them. You can
empower and connect to others humanity, to be an effective communicator. Objectifying
people and protecting yourself, makes you useless. In general, many people in
companies with great ideas can’t readily speak out their mind, and can’t play company
political games well. Companies too often across all industries reward self-confidence
and self-entitled privilege. The man that can walk into his bosses’ office and ask for a
promotion or wage increase, gets that much more than those that don’t ask. Blame for
not asking is placed on the workers, and not the company culture. The sad thing is, that
the people getting promotions, bonuses and higher wages are rarely the best workers,
nor even that bright.

People need to learn how to communicate, be rewarded for good
communication, and be held accountable for bad communication. Another failure
of communication is that workers and bosses in companies, begin to focus more on
protecting themselves, than working on the overall mission of a company. Most
communication is a sea of self-protection, drowning out all useful communication. A
culture of politics and self-interest sets in. People send completely useless emails to
cover their own asses. Company group chats have no real substance in them, and
people avoid making waves. Most email is never read. The goal of sending a message to

someone, is that they read it and the time it took was worth the amount out of help it
provided.

The key to communication and a good email, is just 2 simple rules. You can apply this to
all of life, and into nearly everything you ever do.

1. Communicate in a way that you like, and think is good.
a. Hold yourself up to your own standards.
2. Communicate what is useful for the person receiving
a. Get out of saying things that are only about you, and focus on the person
you are communicating with.

People get lost in not knowing how to format an email or make it look good. Most
everyone already knows what looks good, because they like the style of certain emails
more than others. People need to trust their own judgement and apply it. Short, logical,
to the point emails, with clear key points, with clear formatting, etc are better. If you
like emails with color, use color. If you like teddy bears being sent to you, and think the
other person will value them, send them. Take a risk, and in time things will work out
towards better communication. Self-confidence tempered with common sense can go a
long way. This part of your personality that judges your own thinking is that voice in
your head you most associate with your own identity, is one you need to listen to, in
order to make more clear and presentable writing. Make it something you want to read.
People have to develop their own inner voice, and trust themselves more. If you actually
like another person’s style then use it. This is very different than copying a style to kiss
up to your boss.

Getting over yourself and focusing on creating value for others with sincere connections
based on their needs and feelings, is a fundamental skill for communication and life.
People get lost in their own needs and minds. Once you can develop yourself, you need
to get out of your own head, and get your words and ideas into other people’s heads.
You have to start thinking about what people want to hear, and how they hear things.
This part of your personality is more like your conscience and an eye that sits outside
you that can more directly engage the world, and criticizes you the way you imagine the
world criticizes. This part of you internalizes the voices of others, and is also the voice
you use to communicate and connect to others. You know what part of your personality
this is, and you just need to use it properly with your inner voice, to create proper
writing.

The time you give others, is your respect for others. If you don’t give any real thought or
time to people, you don’t respect them, and can’t develop any sincere communication
with them.

THE TECH.

If people reject an email they receive they can get a list of reasons they didn’t read it
nor reply. If it isn’t read, this should reflect on the sender, and be tracked as a form of
communication performance data on the sender. An overall large amount of emails
unread, and not in a few specific cases, illustrates a clear problem, where that person
needs help. Being able to identify those problems, and create targeted training, becomes
the basis of the technology.They can give back absolutely brutal feedback. “Unreadable”
“Useless Rubbish” “Covering their own ass” “Nothing to do with anything we are doing”
“Disturbing”, etc. Can be quick shallow reasons, or even more deep and specific ones. As
a pattern emerges across all their messages, in the feedback, we can target people’s

problems with specific training. The system will learn and grow with us. The choices
people get to critique an email, will evolve and be targeted based on what an AI thinks
may be faulty with it. AI analysis of text is improving very quickly. It can target the
emotional tone of different words and language patterns. Angry emails can easily be
identified, and people can be given “Is too angry”, as an option. The person sending an
email, won’t know who rejected their email, just that overall in the aggregate they have
a problem.

People need brutal feedback and accountability, supported with great online training, so
they can know what to do, and not just be told what is wrong. People that communicate
well and contribute to the systems development and knowledge the most, can be
rewarded. It will certainly stand out in an OpenHR machine-learning-big-data based
evaluation system, and raise the value of that worker. “Nice” people, that can add to
teams, can also stand out. Raising the level of communication so more “shy” members
speak out, takes more than a management suggestion box. At some level this basic
idea, has to be super powered with technology, and not just through the boss.

OPEN AG: GMOS ARE GOOD -ORGANIC FOOD INDUSTRY BAD

•

companies that sell them.

•

The more value to our humanity that we can see being added in tangible
specific ways by the GMO industry, the more we can embrace this
frightening new technology into our lives.

•

Create jobs, create new business, make us healthier, save the
environment, bring nature and life into our cities, lift up continents of
people, end world hunger, create beauty all around us, and the promise
of GMOs can be made real and be embraced.

We can design food that is vastly tastier, healthier, cheaper, and better for the
environment, with advanced genetic engineering, and new technologies for where and
how we grow food. Urban farming and vertical farming can be integrated with high
technology into buildings in cities. This will take farming out of farm lands, and free up
more land for nature. Urban environments will be the most able to capitalize on GMO
plants and add an increased health benefit to the cities, with more plants cleaning the air
and homes of people. We need to realize that nature is for nature and that cities are for
people. We need to separate our food supply from nature and create it in the cities we

use, the more we can create the future, protect the earth, and live happier healthier
lives. People will more readily embrace GMOs in urban farming, that they can see and
feel in their everyday life.

Organic food is a scam, and has negative environmental value, and negative health
value. GMOs are the future and the best technology for human beings. All the science,
facts, common sense, and reality back that up. Organic food is great for spoiled first
world rich people, and a nightmare for people that are actually spending large
percentages of their income on food. Most of the useful tech in the organic food industry

GMO companies though have not really helped their case. They need to sell themselves

uses less resources, and even tastes better, will be an unstoppable commercial success
for all humanity.

A START UP TECH REVOLUTION

GMOs don’t have to be driven by large multinational corporations distant from the

millions, of farm start-ups. Farming needs start-ups, in all the craziest of places we can
never imagine. We need a tech revolution here.

If the companies doing all this are fundamentally open and we can see how they do their

resist. Our farms are not integrated into our world and most of the work is done by

A GMO company that existed as an open platform, that helped third world countries,

sharing between companies. Like the drug industry and few big tech companies, the

focused on the empowerment and betterment of humanity.

When it comes to space and farming off world, all this tech can help make that possible,
and create inspiration in how we make things. When designing a system, simpler ways
can seem more expedient, and the only inspiration and drive to make it better at all
levels, comes from a far-reaching vision of the future and adding fundamental value for
of all humanity. The usefulness in well-made and well-thought-out tech, will pay off over
the long run. How to grow food on a space station can empower the people of the earth
with new and amazing technology.

OPEN ENERGY: NUCLEAR POWER AND FRACKING

-We built the wrong things from the Manhattan project and the Nasa Space
race. It is time to fix that mistake, for the future and destiny of mankind-

We need Manhattan project for the worlds energy supply, with competing countries from

This project needs to be driven by capitalism and innovation, rather than fascism like
drove it before. An innovative capitalist start-up culture with many possibilities must be
central to such an undertaking. Nuclear power is the best option. There are too many
regulations and laws stopping research and innovation. Companies will invent a solution
if we create a safe space for them to do research. There are different competing ways to
make safe and abundant nuclear power, that all need to be explored, to see which can
be the cheapest and safest to implement on a mass scale. We need a solution that can
be mass manufactured in assembly line factories, and deliver power to the world as fast
as possible, without inherent risks and dangers, such as nuclear weapons.

Science and technology lost its way and it hinders the future. When we align ourselves
to the right path again, we will see a new golden age of science, and discovery. The
Manhattan project brought to humanity a fundamental human tragedy in nuclear
weapons and even greater tragedy in a belief that government funded science could
solve any great problem. The Manhattan project is one of the reasons that science has
slowly died in our modern era, as government took an ever-increasing role in funding
and advancing science. The Apollo program was the peak of government backed fascist
science system, that in effect ended free and modern science in America after the Moon
landing. People can admire the Apollo mission by ignoring the rather glaring fascism to it
all: nationalism, militarism, propaganda, Nazi scientists, Nazi plans, mythology, worldwide military dominion, massive government spending, corrupt connections to
corporations. It made a system to rain down nuclear hell fire on any place on Earth and

launch a satellite system to watch over everything and guide weapons, as the primary
goal.

In the years that followed, science turned to government funding to feed its budgets,
and in turn altered its findings to fit the needs of an ever-expanding government and its
power. They find new causes to organize government power around that in turn fund
ever expanding scientific studies, across multiple disciplines. Climate change is the
natural evolution of this fascism and the seeking of totalitarian power. At the root The
Manhattan Project, The Apollo Program, and Climate Change, are one connected
ideology and story. It is a story of failed science, bad technology, fundamental
inhumanity, and a dying world. We need to undo this mistake in history and build the
great things nuclear power has for the world.

Before we can bring nuclear power to the world, we need other power sources, and
alternatives to coal and oil. Saving the environment takes immediate things that can
work now. The soot and dirt from Chinese pollution is the biggest danger to the Earth
and human life now. Fracking can replace coal and oil. Modern coal power plants can be
cheaply and easily converted to run on natural gas, and thus not need massive new
infrastructure or spending. Natural gas can be turned into alcohol (methanol) with some
cheap and simple refinement. This fuel can run in gasoline burning cars that we use
today, with some cheap and easy modifications to the engine. China needs natural gas
now, to get rid of all the coal burning. Gas is much cleaner to burn. It is better for the
planet and human life. Fracking has dangers and can even cause earthquakes. We need
to balance out the dangers of all fuels, and realize that only fracking and natural gas can
have an immediate impact on the Earth, where things are most critical, and immediately
help the quality of life for real people. Business and not socialism leads to the future.

CHAPTER 3. THE ETHICAL CREATION OF CYBERNETICS AND AI

“Act in such a way that you treat humanity, whether in your own person or in the
person of another, always at the same time as an end and never simply as a
means.” — Immanuel Kant, Groundwork of the Metaphysics of Morals (1785)

Ethics at its root is a constant emotional process of finding and accepting sincere
humanity in others. People are not things. You must try to treat humans as something
fundamentally human and never as a thing to use for your own ends. We must respect
our own humanity, and treasure that sense of truth in ourselves. Finding fundamental
humanity in others, different from you is frightening and requires deep openness, and
the capacity to change and grow. To be human is to have a will to live and strive to be
more than you were before, in each and every moment. Life is a choice in all moments
between living and dying. We must choose, continuously and constantly in every single
action we take in life, and can only know life from death, with absolute honesty with
yourself. Honesty is developed in a connection with another person, and accepting them
fully for who they are as a person. Knowing other people and relationships are inherently
messy, inter-tangled and complex. The process of ethics is not easily contained in one’s
persons minds and cognitive abilities. We need help from others and deep connections to
others, to be good, rather than be consumed by our intellectual vanity. Ethics are the
process of creating the future for human life, beyond your own self, and from your own
self.

A HEROES JOURNEY

Humans see themselves as the heroes of their own story, and use stories to model
themselves from and into. Classic imagery and ideas of beauty, self-sacrifice, romantic
love, heroism, valor, honor, inspire souls. Most of fiction is just writers projecting out
their own fantasies. We have this fantasy universe all around us, that we can project
ourselves into, depending on who we admire and want to be like. What it means to be a
hero, is the way in which we live; the rules and principles we live by, in this world; it is
the people we inspire and build up. Real people, real heroes, are far more human,
flawed, and vulnerable, than we readily accept. Ethics is about who we make into
heroes, and how we envision the future.

•

Shows of heroic doctors, spies, FBI agents, lawyers, cops, fireman, saving people,
make up most of TV. These people are all nearly super human at their job, and
portray this level of near mastery, that few in reality even remotely live up to.

•

Watching sports is just a heroic fantasy story, where we imagine ourselves into
sporting events, and achieving amazing accomplishments, or even having that
star as our lover.

•

Reality TV stars created far more human and flawed heroes for people to admire.
It is too real and too human for many people. They can’t accept ideals outside
their own.

•

Christ is the embodiment of a perfect man struggling to be the ultimate hero and
role model for all mankind. We conceive of and see Christ from our own inner
visions of our heroic inner story. “What Would Jesus Do” is a simple thought
exercise that connects you to your own inner vision that structures your reality.

KANT’S ETHICS REBORN

Ethics in their most noble sense are rules for human behavior, that would or should
apply to everyone. All cultures are ethical systems. Ethics creates long lasting societies,
and a more prosperous life for those that live in a society where people follow them.
Ethical cultures are more enduring, and will survive better. Survival that is enhanced
through culture is ethics and measured in degrees of civilization. There is a great
German philosopher called Immanuel Kant. He wrote some very influential and very
idealized books on ethics. He came up with the “Categorical Imperative”, as thought
exercise for making ethical rules. It doesn’t work in practical reality.

“Act only according to that maxim by which you can at the same time will that it
should become a universal law.”
— Immanuel Kant, Groundwork of the Metaphysics of Morals (1785)

•

All ethics are simply rules. And we do a simple thought exercise
o

Imagine if you had a rule that everyone had to follow.

o

If the rule makes the world worse, it is bad, if the rule makes the world
better, it is good.

•

Two kinds of ethics exist, the categorical imperative and the hypothetical
imperative.
o

Categorical Imperative: “You should…because…”

o

Hypothetical Imperative: “If you want …then do…”

o

To explain them as simple as possible; the former is judging good and
bad, and the latter judging better or worse.

o

The hypothetical imperative is the process, and the categorical imperative
is more like the goal or standard that you make things by and never really
achieve. One is reality and the other is unattainable idealism.

All rules are hypothetical imperatives, are flawed Categorical imperatives in process. If
we keep refining what it is we want and the rules that we have to govern that, then we
can more and more approach ideal ethical ideas. The idealized categorical imperative
becomes the idealized world we want to live in, and often drives us to create false nonfunctional rules that lead to utopia the fastest. Reality exists and it always comes back,
because human nature is unchanging, nasty, and brutal.

The hypothetical imperative is just a simple logic exercise, you say what you want, and
do what will logically lead to that result. I want to eat; I go eat. You have a desire and
you act on it. As we get what we think we want, we realize we want something different
than that. We don’t even know we have these desires unless we live in this world a full
life and highly stable civilizations, and have basics needs fulfilled. Our sense of hunger
can reflect moral truths. The “best” chicken nuggets are GMO-Free, Fair trade, free
range, sales taxed, import duties paid, Gluten free, American made, Christian owned,
charity supporting, equal opportunity employing, law abiding, troop supporting, Olympic
sponsoring, and dipped in awesomeness sauce that will make good women want to
marry me more.

At some point a fixed rule that makes things better will eventually make things worse.
Laws evolve as society evolves. “An Eye for an Eye”, is a very ethical law in a society
where people feel the need to take one life or more, for an eye. It is not very ethical in a
world where people don’t take revenge and kill others freely. Creating more civilized
people by domesticating them with ethical training doesn’t change the fact that we are
wild animals and savages. As life and civilization become more sacred and cherished, so
does the refinement in how we protect and nurture life itself, and also forget who we
really are for more idealized versions of ourselves.

EVOLVING KANT

Kant’s main problem was his excess idealism, and rigid materialism. He believed in the
literal existence of ethics as a thing, and that since they couldn’t be seen, they had a
near material existence in another plane of reality outside our own observation. Idealism
inherently creates a literal artificial and unobservable reality to base itself on. To believe
in ideals as real things, is to deny reality and actual living. Kant’s ethics, with
adjustments, need just reality and no idealistic underpinnings to really work. It is nearly
impossible to define something as absolutely good or bad. This is idealism, that only
exists in theories and people’s imaginations as real. We can approach ethical rules, and
never actually achieve them fully as pure and perfect things. Life is messy, and the
process is a constant struggle. The proper study of ethics is about better and worse.
Ethics is a process, more than set defined absolute truth.

1. You do something
2. see the results,
3. adjust,
4. try to be better
5. never settle on any result as 100% correct

This is still too idealistic, though moving towards a better explanation. There isn’t any
really set or proper explanation for anything in reality. “Truth” is all based in probability
and continuous improvements. We will never live in a perfect good world. We can only
improve slowly on the world we live. When we evolve towards better systems, we only
find more problems and more things we need to adapt to. Ethics are born out of

survival, and are based on what works and doesn’t work. People can control ourselves
and the reality around us, in a better and more consistent way, with evolving ethics. We
can judge our ethics by how well they contribute to a better society and world, that
actually works, and is more civilized. Kant made an extreme rule that we should never
lie, and in that rule, we can find his failure and redemption.

“NEVER LIE” REBORN

If you want something from someone, then tell that person what you want
from them.

All ethical rules need to be positive and hypothetical. Absolute and negative rules lead to
poor thinking and a breakdown of real ethics. People don’t want to be told what they
shouldn’t and should do all the time, by morally preening hypocrites. If ethics are about
intentions, and not lying is ethical, then it is in ourselves that we need to be honest, in
order to be ethical. Self-honesty is the root of ethics, morality, good intentions, and
living for a positive future. We lie to ourselves constantly, and hide from the reality of
who we are and the actions we have done. We hide from the very goodness and
wholeness inside ourselves. That capacity to know and feel shame at one’s self is the
essence of being human and good. Addiction consumes people’s lives because they lie to
themselves, and are consumed by self-hate at the imperfect petty-monsters inside
themselves. Self-honesty is a never-ending process of self-discovery and growth, that
heals us and brings us closer to sincere honest intentions.

We must share with another human being and be unashamed of ourselves in their
presence, in order to learn and grow in ourselves. Only when we can be wholly honest

with another can we see ourselves reflected back at ourselves honestly and accept who
we are, while we in turn are forced to accept them, and see in them all the things we
reject in ourselves, and need to love.

People themselves don’t like to tell people what they really want because it makes them
vulnerable and human. We don’t know what we really want until we start to act out and
get what we think we want, and then adjust our goals with trial and error. Good
intentions can’t be made real until people externalize their intentions to others, and are
direct in their goals. Just saying directly what you want, precisely in an exact moment,
can be a transformative experience, and profoundly difficult to do, with even the most
basic of things. You know things to be right and wrong, and say nothing out of fear. The
exact words to say won’t be clear, and the exact way to do it won’t be obvious. Show
your real intentions and see reality from fantasy. You need to be vulnerable to someone
and connect your desires and self to a reality greater than yourself. People can never be
better for us unless we ask them to be better. Relationships and truth is messy and filled
with conflict. If someone loves you, they will listen and change, if you can listen and
accept them fully.

The difference between destructive and healthy relationships is fundamentally simple
and easy. Real relationships drive us to be more honest with ourselves, and drive us to
constantly challenge our very sense of identity for something truer. Unhealthy
relationships support our lies to our own selves, and give comfort to our weakness and
cowardice; they turn themselves into objects. Our assumptions about others are the lies
we tell ourselves so that person becomes more acceptable to us, and we don’t actually
have to listen to them nor understand them. You can test how honest you are with a
person easily, by telling them all the presumptions you have about them, and listening
to their response and accepting it. We all lie when we have assumptions about people

that we base our perceptions of them, and we don’t tell them. Good intentions can only
be good, if they are driven by constant self-honesty, and a connection to another
person, that challenges us to accept them fully as a human being to us.

JOSHUA’S ETHICAL SYSTEM

“A rational being must always regard himself as giving laws either as member or as
sovereign in a kingdom of ends which is rendered possible by the freedom of will.”

— Immanuel Kant, Groundwork of the Metaphysics of Morals (1785)

Finding and developing a rule system to govern ethics is a continuing and difficult
process. There is no perfect or finished version. Only you can do it for yourself. My ethics
exist in a sequential system. I started with my most deep-rooted principle, and then
found a weakness in it, added a rule, found a weakness in that, added another rule, and
so on. As my sense of who I am, and what I want expands, my ethical rules expand. I
learned them in this order, as I lived my life.

THE HARD SOUL
HARD SELF: Self-Identity Ethics. Personal power, logic, and consistency (nonAgreeable non-Conscientiousness)
•
•
•

Rule 1. “If you see something that is wrong, and you have the power to do
something about it, you must do it, no matter the cost to yourself or your life. “
Rule 2. “Develop you power to its fullest.” Respect who and what you are
fundamentally. With great responsibility comes great power.
Rule 3. “Only ask of others what you would ask of yourself.” Follow the golden
rule of leaders and generals. Don’t use people as ends in themselves to serve
your needs. Have the courage to do what you would ask of others, and have the
courage to ask of others what you need.

SOFT OTHERS: External Agreeableness of Values. Community, Society, Duty, Sacrifice
(Agreeable Conscientiousness)
•

•

•

Rule 4. “You can learn from all people” Find within all people something you
profoundly respect, and engage them fundamentally from that space, and build
all relationships from that.
Rule 5. “Lead with your weakest foot forward” Incorporate into yourself that
which you respect in others, into yourself. Face your pride and failings. While you
can be superior to another, don’t connect to them through that elitism.
Rule 6. Seek out and connect to people you respect. Live a connected and pure
life. Purity, purpose, direction, health, and destiny.

THE SOFT SOUL
SOFT SELF: Inner Self-Agreeableness. Personal Morality (Agreeable nonConscientiousness)
•
•
•

rule 1’. “Do things that make you happy” do something that will truly make you
happy. a real dream.
Rule 2’. “Know what truly makes you happy” respect yourself fully. Never get
dark or lost.
Rule 3’. “Do what you are told to do by those you respect.” Only one person can
be maximally happy at a given moment.

HARD OTHERS: External Identity Structures. Hierarchy and leadership of a structured
world. Collective categorical group identities (Non-Agreeable Conscientiousness)
•
•
•

Rule 4’. “Find those that will obey and follow you.”
Rule 5’. “Lead with power and strength to give people certainty and security”
Rule 6’. “Show respect to get respect” Treat others the way you want to be
treated.

EXPANDED EXPLANATION:

1. Responsibility- Do and say everything you feel you must do, regardless of the
anxiety, and the consequences you imagine. Anxiety arises when we don’t act.
We can train people to overcome anxiety by setting small tasks that can be
overcome and merely cause anxiety. A person can learn to face the uncertainty in
themselves and find power they didn’t believe they had, and realize this can
apply to much larger sets of things, and thus, build the self-confidence to conquer
fear and accept failure.
2. Self-respect- There are no such things as real victims. One must develop one’s
abilities to the fullest. You must become as powerful in oneself as you are

capable. This development must always be moving forward, even with setbacks.
The speed of this development will be defined by reality. Even people with severe
limitations, have certain points they can develop at any time and in any situation.
Even in prison, one can grow. There are no excuses. There is only choosing to be
responsible or not responsible for the life you want to live.
3. Leadership (pay your dues)- With responsibility and power comes an obligation to
lead and define reality around oneself. We must only ask of others what we would
ask of ourselves. This is a variation of the golden rule built around respect and
not compassion. We learned to do and respect the shit jobs that we didn’t want to
do. You don’t shove them on others, when they are our duty and responsibility to
do.
4. Respect for others. (Sincere Respect for others). We must always believe in the
abilities of others. All people have something they are good at, and we must
respect that ability. Engage people from the fundamental strengths in them, that
you respect in them. If you don’t respect a person at a root level in something,
then no sincere connection can develop, and at some level you just view them as
a thing to use.
5. Learn from others. (Teachers) All people can be our teacher in something. While
we may respect another’s abilities, we may think we are still better than them in
all things. We must get very focused. Forrest Gump was a genius in one thing,
and those that could see that and respect that, prospered, in the story.
6. Purity. (the hard work). While we must be open to all people and seek the best in
them. We must also cut away the bad and minimize exposure to bad influences
and habits that bring us down. When we grow beyond people, we must honor
what they taught us, feel gratitude, and leave. Our destiny is our habits

CASE STUDY: DEVELOPMENT OF CHILDREN WITH ETHICAL SYSTEMS

A man’s 7-year-old son comes to him and says he wants to make an iPhone game. The
boy is very curious, and his father is in the app development industry and knows all the
things needed to do this. The father sees ability in his son, but also knows apps are
hard. He wants to encourage his son, and develop his abilities, while not having his son
do something impossible. He needs to narrow the goal to something his son can do,
while also respecting the goal he son set for himself to do. He needs to begin where his
son can do something. He gets an iMac for his kid with the basic game making tools in it,
and then gets basic platforms his kid can learn in step by step. Now he also has to make
sure his son is paying his dues and doing real work. If the child has tasks set for them,
that they can do, want to do, and are hard, they are likely to overcome with enough
time and emotional support. The boy will need to seek help when he really can’t do
something, and it is up to the parent to know when it is ok to delegate and not the kid.
It needs to be based in gratitude and not entitlement.

If the father gets all this expensive stuff for them in order to empower his kid and not
satisfy guilt, the kid can feel gratitude and not be spoiled. Guilt will drive a parent to
permit spoiled behavior, and not empowerment, because they are too lazy to really care
and focus on their kid. Secretly the father is probably guilty about something and when
the kid just goofs around and is being naughty the dad may cave in, and be happy to
see their kid smiling playing a game, rather than making a game, because they deep
down just wanted their kid to accept them, and not empower their child. The father must
be strong here, and show respect to his son’s abilities and not secretly think the kid can’t
and just did this to buy his kids love.

He should investigate what his son finds interesting in games and look at the games he
likes, and basically get to really know his child, and connect to the child’s ability to
discern quality. The parent has to respect their kids “taste” in something, or the parent
won’t really want to invest in that kid. If your 7-year-old cooks the most amazing food
you ever tasted, you will certainly have no problem investing in them learning to be
chef, if they tell you that is what they want. Find the specific aspects in each game that
he is drawn to: art, gameplay, style, tone, etc. Keep asking the child why, so they think
deeper on specific aspects and develop their own understanding of good and bad. As the
reasons get tighter and more defined, actually work and design can take shape.
