IN THE BEGINNING

Cultures don’t have to be so nice to evolve into the dominant one. In human beings,
there seems to a be a cultural or even biological evolution, that developed after we
became sentient and was different than the other sentient beings that evolved. The way
we evolve as humans, is different than the way animals evolve. Common people’s
conceptions of evolution relate more to the projecting of human evolution on to the
world, and religious people’s rejection of scientific evolution is driven by how it doesn’t
describe humanity. Common notions of evolution are that is that is progressive, and
where things can be more evolved and less evolved. It is more like some racist code
words to make certain people more or less human than others, based on their genetics,
and where more evolved species are more human like.

I hypothesis that the essence of being human is based in our innate drives to commit
genocide. Humans evolved to slaughter their competition, and this changed the very
nature of how evolution expressed itself on earth. Over a long period of time an instinct
to kill for collective purposes, could lie at humanities success as a species. As this
instinct evolved, it created the very differences between humans and other humanoid
species, and eventually evolve into the very driving force that created civilization. It
wouldn’t just be a single killing gene that popped up in the gene pool. It would require a

set of genes that evolved over time, and in relationship to evolving cultural practices. It
isn’t a singular drive, or singular way of thinking. Culture itself shapes genetic evolution.
Culture defines in groups and out groups. It creates a form of self-domestication, by
favoring certain kinds of social behavior arising out of genetics that are conducive to
living in a culture bearing society. Genes shape culture, and culture shapes genes. We
domesticated humanity with the ultimate domestication adaptation of using targeted
mass genocide. We killed of those that didn’t fit in, on a global and not just local scale.
Humans are a “global” species, with the power to kill of whole groups of people for a
moral purpose.

Over time, this genocidal inclination evolved into a civilization gene. We developed an
instinct to define what is human, and not human. “Humanity” is directly born out a
history against inhuman people. It could have begun with repugnance and disgust at
certain physical appearances in people. A drive to create healthier and viable members,
could evolve into a collective capacity to commit genocide on those different than us,
and in time evolve into the driving force that created civilization and civilized people. The
drive to make humans look more like children, could be such a connected thing. Humans
select more childlike appearances and minds for survival as a collective culture bearing
species, because it makes them more receptive to learning and fitting in with a larger
group. Then later we could evolve a trigger to kill more adult like appearances found in
“primitive” looking people. A simple aesthetic preference could shape a great deal of
human brain development, and favor child-like minds over more set adult ones. This
preference made us more malleable into large groups and thus more collectively
powerful.

We as humans kill all sentient life that is not the same as us, we have an extra urge to
kill that which is most similar and yet different. Anything that is too close to us as

humans, but not human, we kill. A certain genocidal instinct seems to be possible, and
existing in human beings, maybe not all people, but enough to be a driving force to kill
off other competing peoples. This may be an evolutionary dead end, and if we really are
so genocidal, we may be more likely to destroy ourselves, than a more peaceful
humanity that lived in nature, and adapted with multiple species of humanity. However,
a peaceful collection of species would never grow in size to create social groupings of
people numbering in the billions.

Silly tangent
This could be the real original sin in our creation, that dooms us. It also could
have evolved to its peak form, at the exact same time, as the moment original
sin appeared in the book of genesis: 6,500 years ago. This instinct itself may
have evolved over 40,000 years into what we see now.

What made man able to create civilization itself, was a deeply dark change in the
nature of human beings. Civilized man and stone age man, may almost be
different species. Adam and Eve came to kill the inhumans, while also bringing
the light of civilization and new age to man!

In a group of humans only a certain percentage of people need this inclination, for them
to go out and slaughter our competition for the singular position of sentient life on this
planet. Or you might say, we have an inclination to kill off “wild” humans. There aren’t
really any wild humans left, so the desire to kill them, is not felt, and thus this latent
instinct not triggered so directly and purely, almost ever, within large percentages of the
human population. What we think of as genocide in our gentle world, may not compare
anything at all to the sheer butchery of the past. Humans have this interesting quality in

the evolutionary record. Whenever another human like species of animal, came into
contact with humans, they quickly died off. There wasn’t just one sentient species on
earth, at one time. Many existed at once, and we went around the world killing them off,
with gorillas buried away in deep dark jungles, and thus escaping a total genocidal
massacre.

When we see 3d animation that looks too human, it triggers a revulsion in us. Similarity
is cute to us, until it become too human, and yet not human looking. Androids that
looked very human, would trigger intense violent death on them. AI brains, that seem
too human, will generate intense revulsion, and a desire to smash them. Possibilities,
possibilities, possibilities. Technology that becomes too invasive too wise, too knowing,
will be smashed to death. We as humans will rule supreme.

•

Technology that does not bow to our vanity, will not exist.

•

Our humanity is a self-fulfilling birthright to absolute power.

EVOLVING CIVILIZATION

This possible way of thinking, that exists in people, where we kill by instinct, could be
our evolutionary dead end. Better possibilities could have been a species that learned to
get along with the other sentient beings of the earth, and create a grand harmonious
multispecies society.

Or

This cruelty could lie at the foundation of civilization itself, and we form into a large
complex, super stable societies through it. We have to kill off the more animalistic
humans in order to have more stability and larger units of organization, which can create
more complex levels of organization.

We feel guilty for this emotion inside of us, this imperfection, this savagery. We want to
edit it out of us as humans and or deny its very existence. We want a culture that can lift
us up beyond the absolute killing and brutality, that made life and civilization possible.
We want to imagine a world where we don’t kill off distant others, to push forward our
own group. Our inner vanity at our own idealistic perfection is born from absolute
aggression and brutality towards others.

At the deepest levels our very desire for peace, and our idealism, may itself, be
the very heart of an instinct to kill and to commit genocide, the instinct to
preserve and grow that which is human inside of us.

NOMADS AND FARMERS:

Civilization is more than just a cultural adaptation, of new technology and new ways to
organize human beings. Civilized human beings have different biology than humans who
weren’t civilized. Humans civilized themselves down different paths of nomads and
farmers. Those that domesticated animals and those that domesticated plants, evolved
different cultures, and different biology’s, to eat their different diets. They also seem to
think a bit different, and organize themselves differently. Different levels of aggression
are acceptable in different cultures. Certain hormones levels, can have different levels of

survival in different cultures. Nomadic horseman and farmer villagers, can be very
different in their values, and they may have innate tendencies towards different ways of
thinking and organizing themselves.

As we domestic animals and plants to our needs, we domesticate humans to
our needs.

Often, we have created separate classes of humans to enslave and use as livestock to
serve the dominant group. In general, we just kill off the too wild of us, the too savage,
and those unable to live in large societies. We capture and enslave sub-human groups to
serve us, and domesticate them like we do plants and animals. The process of slavery
and domestication of humans probably developed before we domesticated plants and
animals. To be human is to be domesticated to serve others humans, and function in
social groups. As social environments change, the needs of domestication change. It
takes biological adaptations to live in large cities of humans. Governments/warlords cull
us to serve their needs at particular times. A genocidal instinct orients itself towards
collective centralized power, and individual self-preservation. A singular individual would
survive better with brainwashed domesticated humans serving them, and could then
breed more widely than others. Variations of such social interaction exist in great apes,
and the variations of these behaviors developed in us, in ways that led to more rapid
social and evolutionary development.

Modern man is a genetic mix of farmers and nomads. Nomads raided and raped their
way into the culture and the genetic pool of farmer cultures. All modern cultures evolved
from farmers, save a few like the Vikings. Africa didn’t have the land and climate for
stable farming, and never really evolved more complex stable cultures. Most of Africa’s
history, where farming wasn’t stable, was nomadic animal husbandry, ruled by warlord

societies, of differing levels of stability and complexity, though nothing on the scale of
say ancient China, India, Rome, Persia, Egypt, and the such. A civilization can’t form to
any great size without farming, and the cultural and biological adaptations that come
with it.

The poor civilizations of north and south America didn’t evolve with such intense
infectious diseases, as the rest of the world, and died off from the very first contact, with
the much larger and connected lands of Asia, Africa, and Europe. Immunity is a form of
evolutionary adaptation for civilized peoples, because infectious diseases grow in denser
human communities. Most infectious diseases come from China, through history, where
people lived in the largest groupings of people ever in human history, now and through
all of Chinas history. China had multiple great rivers, and the largest farmlands possible.
Disease is a great defense for intruders into societies where they have no immunity.
Disease itself is a weapon against less civilized peoples, and confers great advantages on
domesticated humans. The more social people, would also have a greater propensity to
survive outbreaks due to being cared for by others, so that the more asocial and violent,
would more readily die off.

China evolved a culture to manage such a massive area and population. By nature, only
one culture would ever rule this region. It is a very hard region to rule and keep. The
sheer size of the area requires that one group of a massive size to rule it all, and
Chinese civilization evolved to create a unified massive society capable of occupying
such a region. It required a brutal domestication of the people and culture, to install a
dominant centralized authority. Surrounding this large centralize region, were more
isolatable regions that developed and enriched the main region, or were raiders of it. In
countries like Japan with more isolatable regions, there existed more feudalism and
distinction between varying lords. It was just too hard to invade and conquer another

part of Japan, with such massive mountains. Greek civilization formed with many varying
kinds of people because every single Greek island could be its own country, with its own
laws, and that created the basis of western civilization and its core ideas.

Cultural evolution is not just how big you can get, though it is important. The Chinese
were one of the most civilized people in history. A culture also needs complexity, and not
just authority dominating over it. It needs new ideas, mutations, to grow and evolve.
Large unchanging societies will die off and stagnate. China existed in a symbiotic
relationship with its nomadic neighbors, who themselves shaped and defined Chinese
history, with many Chinese people actually being descendants of these people. “History”
has little to do with what really happened. If the Chinese redefined their history and
identity to include its nomadic identity, it would redefine cultural myths and self-identity.
The Mongols, the Huns, and Turkic people, all are part of the identity and history of what
is to be Chinese. They now exist as citizens in China, and yet are not fully integrated into
the legacy, culture and history of what it is to be Chinese. The variations of culture that
surrounded China, assimilated into the main Chinese culture, and created the very
vitality that helped it survive longer than any other civilization in history.

The Irish had to shape an identity from rape, conquest, pirate raiders,
enslavement, and imperialism.

Genocide though is part of being human. And it feels deeply at odds with this innate
morality and divinity we feel in us as human beings, and seems underlay most all of our
relationships. Feelings are real things, and not just something arising from pure animal
emotions and desires. We feel guilt, and these feelings exist in “humanity” across all
planets. Civilization itself is driven by a different form of evolution than what came
before. If it is dead end or an improvement, I don’t know. It at one level, creates a soft,

gentle idealist pure human, and yet gives birth to that by slaughtering all wild humans,
and domesticating human beings themselves, along with the land, plants and animals.
All is bent to serve a singular will for survival of some kind.

Progress, Domestication, Civilization, Genocide, may all be words for the same thing, at
different times. Progressives of the early 20th century advocated genocide and eugenics
as a moral imperative to make the world a better place, by sterilizing inferior races and
people. It was what “science” found to be correct, and morally enlightened people
pushed the most violent beliefs. Where we find the most noble and civilized people in
history, we find them killing, enslaving, and domesticating human beings at
correspondingly large scales. At some level, many of the kindest and most idealistic
people harbor such thoughts of dominion and murder. It is just being “human”. The
more progressive, civilized, or advanced one imagines themselves, the more they
probably want to kill people unlike themselves. This is how more developed people win
through history, and if they really are better, they can win more readily. A zero-sum
game to the death shaped most of human history and development.

THE POLITICS OF LEFT AND RIGHT.

I have a 6 dichotomy system to explain all of politics and human cognition that
will not be included in this book. 3 of those can correlate to one’s political
orientation more precisely. I am just going to discuss one of them, and in a very
simple way.

Part of what it is to be human is not to love everyone. To evolve we have to love our
own, more than others. At the most basic level, politics can be described along these
ideas. We as humans have innate variations in how much we love our own, and how
much we love outsiders. Forming a stable group that can survive requires intense culture
and close connections to those around us. Deep bonds of family, community, and
country, can hold a people together, and allow them to survive through the innate
difficulties of life. This instinct is at odds with the overall trend of greater stability and
greater complexity. Larger complex societies more closely interlinked with high stability,
will survive longer and align with the very forces the universe.

“Conservatives”/Right Wing/Capitalism

They form tight smaller bands of people. This is an excellent way to survive.
o

These groups of people are heartier and stronger.

o

They can fight man for man much better, than large farming like
communities.

o

Risk taking, bravery, and dying for others are ingrained ethical patterns.

•

Conservatives by nature, don’t seem to want to live in large groupings of people.

They have more intense social bonds to those around them, and want to be left
alone by the outside.

Optional: a philosophical sensitive explanation
Conservatism is obsessed with first causes, and building the logic of how things
come to be from their first principles. This in a material sense is a fixation on the
initial ground state of the universe, and the values one could build from nothing,
or from a universal god that created the whole the universe from nothing. Nondeterminism and mathematics oriented.

Progressive liberals are obsessed with the end. Their logic of how things work is
constructed from perceiving the final result. This is called teleological thinking.
They project their own identity into things to form a whole. The universe is a
singular entity with purpose and direction. History evolves towards an end that is
fulfilling to human life. In the physics analogy they see the expanding evolving
universe, moving towards something. Determinism and teleology.

This may have origins in the beginning of man’s development of civilization, in nomads
and farmers, or it may not. Conservatism seems to correlate well with nomadic societies
and how they adapted to survive, and liberal left-wing correlates well with grand cities of
farming civilizations. They are a 2 different cultural species of human beings, that are
now intermixed together. People can still overall be born with innate mental preferences
for one way of thinking over the other, down to how their very hormones deal with
things. Left and Right political thinking are innate features of a human being, that don’t
just arise from their upbringing. Two very liberal parents in a very liberal city, can have
2 very liberal kids, and one very conservative kid. Sort of like being gay, in a family of
straight people, and everyone around you is straight. There is science and basic practical
reason, to back this up.

This central division in humanity may also be innate to all civilized sentient life. We have
an ability to fine tune our own cultural stability and complexity, based on the actual
conditions of the world. The two forces become represented in the very identity of being
human, as reflected in the very laws of the universe. Neither is exactly right or wrong.
Bigger, more powerful, diverse society, vs a smaller more densely connected group with
high stability and trust. Strong culture and society vs strong government. History shows
what happens in extreme societies with high government and low culture, and where
high culture and low government exist. Both are the stuff of nightmares. Living in a
warlord society or a communist/fascist totalitarian society, is at some level cognitive
preference, in choosing which hell you think is better to live in. The answer is not
actually so clear. There isn’t a right answer, but people will think there is one, based on
what they prefer, based on their politics.

Conservatives seek more stability, which leads to smaller, more isolated groupings of
people that are more intensely connected and related to each other. They value a
fundamental internal consistency to reality and self at a fundamental level. The left can
handle increasing in size of societies, with diminishing cultural cohesion, and increasing
chaos. In that chaos and sheer size exists greater opportunity for change that actually
works to come into being. There are more chances for new things to exist in a liberal
society, even though most of what it creates will be rubbish. Most of that chaos is death,
and societal collapse. Early liberal man would have had massive growth and collapse, in
an unending cycle. It was a horrendous way of life, that there was no escape from,
where people just died where they were born.

Civilization and large societies in its beginnings was in no way pretty, or clearly better,
until the age of enlightenment in western Europe. Farming often had booms and busts.

Most human history is just smaller groups taking the food from weaker groups, with the
weaker ones dying off in mass numbers. I would presume far greater happiness in
primitive nomad groups than primitive farming societies. In conservatism lays a
contradiction, they embrace human nature, but reject its evolving reality. A large
society that is ever increasing and mixing, that doesn’t have strong conservative
stabilizing forces, will collapse in chaos. A society not growing and allowing for variation,
will not evolve. Strong cultural institutions and deep loyalties to one’s clan and family,
create highly stable and strong societies, that don’t adapt well, because they lack
constant outside contact, that drives change.

America was a grand fusion of these twin pillars of humanity. The Founding fathers were
a mix of these different ways of thinking, and they worked together, respected each
other, and built the greatest country ever in humanity. The fusionism began in England,
and reached its maturity in America. This fusionism was, for me, the foundation of the
enlightenment beyond the scientific vision of Newton. Human beings could have easily
lived for thousands of more years with no America, and the fundamental changes it
brought to the world. The recent technological revolution of the world was driven by
American culture, that fused conservatism to liberalism.

The American right is a whole other species from the right-wing cultures of many other
countries. Pure strains of it exist, and it is often repressed through American history.
Nativism with intense identity politics that becomes nasty is not really the classic
conservatism Americans embrace. It is however a real and driving force in the world,
that when repressed leads to totalitarian and authoritarian societies, with closed borders
and closed minds.

This evolution was an essential one. No great civilization in the future, can survive

HUMAN COGNITIVE DIVERSITY

Being an extravert or introvert, are innate features in a person, with degrees of variation
in between, there however is an overall defining innate biological component. Aliens will
also have this variation, expressed in some form, in their cognitive capacities. We have
to learn how to use all of this variation in human natures, that enrich us. We have ever
more complex variations between us, that allow us to specialize and be good at different
kinds of thinking, innately. We can organize ourselves, and solve problems, and think
differently, as a way to culturally adapt. We have a cognitive diversity spread across us
biologically, and a share unifying cultural identify, history, and technology to unite us in
a common cause of collective survival.

PART 3 INTRODUCTION:
This part of the book is Hard. I try to deal with the hardest problem ever considered in
the history of humanity, and it may very well be the most important question in all of
reality. With the world, I am living in burning, and the moral foundations of society in
ruins, this is an attempt to change the entire nature of scientific, philosophical and
religious debate, for all time. I am not a theist, an atheist, nor an agnostic. This section
is not science, not theology, and barely philosophy. It is just history and logic.

I attempt to crack the underpinnings to reality, and in the realm of science, describe
what came before the big bang, and why such a question can be answered in real
scientific terms, and how this itself created the conditions of the big bang. I don’t use
magic, I don’t use mysticism. I use logic, hard speculative science, the facts we have,
and imaginative critical thinking. This is an attempt at making hypothesis’s that can lead
to actual scientific experiments and actual new discoveries. The goal is to inspire people
and take a fresh look at the problems in physics and how the results of such new study
could change the world drastically. If this work leads to experiments that completely
disprove it and in the process help lead to a better idea, I will be proud of this work.

SCIENCE IN MY TIME, IMAGINES ITSELF IN A GOLDEN AGE. I SEE IT IN
A DARK AGE.

At the heart of science is a person trying to prove their own imagined model of reality to
be false. This is for all of science’s complexity is its simple genius and profound moral
value in changing the world for the better. To make paradigms that change everything,
you need to see deep models of possible reality in your own head, and in your sense of
self. You really need to believe them to be true, and then go out and create experiments
to falsify these models and ideas. You don’t make experiments to prove things to be
true. You try to disprove it, by making crazy predictions that only your model can
predict, if the predictions are wrong, you have a bad model or you did the experiment
poorly. Testability, falsifiability and a real human connection to an idea, create science.

We have to get teams of people working together with different mental abilities and
using different procedures, to get science working at its very best. The scientific method
has broken down in our modern world very badly, even with its mountain of epic
achievements. Scientific methodologies are at their heart about dealing with human
nature. It is about how to get people to work well together, that don’t get along well,
that think completely differently, and have valid different points of view. There is an
underlying system of rules, procedures, peer review, “laws”, and governing bodies, that
did a lot of great things in the past, that has failed in our current world. Eventually any
formal process will fail because we are human, and there is always more to the story
than we are willing to admit. The root of solution is far more about respecting and
understanding humanity, than it is in some complex philosophical debate about the
meaning of truth. We will all have a different meaning for the word “truth”, and not fully
respect differing views on the subject. Good science challenges one’s own model of
reality and one’s own sense of self. If people aren’t actively trying to disprove

themselves and working together with people different than them, the system will fail.
The system doesn’t reward people for proving themselves utterly wrong. “The 2024
Noble Prize for Honesty goes to…. for completely disproving his life’s work that had
become mainstream belief.”

Science doesn’t have to be impersonal and cold. Our feelings create what we study. The
more we understand our feelings, the more we can push into new frontiers of science
and understanding. The more we can bring our feelings and selves into it, the more we
can attract people to do science and to think more. We can attract and bring in truly
smart people, that will be able to imagine things in new ways, and give us new insights
into how things work. Women don’t have to start thinking like men to be useful, and
their own unique humanity and differences can inspire new insights into the nature of
reality. Science must reclaim its heart, and that pursuit of “truth” will always have man
and our future inside it.

Chapter 9: The Philosophy of Science

The Nature of Science

Science demystifies magic out of the world. This demystification and ripping the magic
back is upsetting. The closer it gets to the origins of life, the universe, and our very
identity the more shocking it becomes. Love is mostly a bunch of very different biological
functions that get labeled love: chemicals, insanity, addiction, reflexes. Love may exist
and in the realm of science it is mostly just collective delusions needing to be peeled
back to show its primitive mechanical nature. The quest for a God with meaning in the
universe, can lead people to be lazy in their scientific explanations, and the desire for
there to be no god, can also blind science. Atheist Scientists, are also driven by many
un-reflected upon desires and impulses that make them prone to believe in absurd
things, like say communism, transhumanism, an earth goddess, eugenics, or the
meaningless of marriage. Theists refuse to challenge things, and refuse to dig deeper
into the origins of things when they challenge the perceived sacredness of things.

Science pushes back the veil of darkness and superstition, it takes the magic out of the
universe. Disease is not caused by ghosts, demons, or bad energy. Trees do not have
feelings. Science pushed magic out of nature. When some scientist tells people that love
doesn’t exist, and is just chemicals, this can make people really mad, and reject science
itself. “Real love” in people may exist, however a great deal of what we call love is just
chemicals, programing, and instincts. It is just mechanical operations that create an
emotional illusion in our brains that is created by neurochemicals and cognitive instincts.

Much of what we feel is just an illusion. Our sense of reality is an illusion. Much of our
very sense of identity and self, isn’t even real. Science can help us see and understand
that. It will one day really understand these things, and this will help people live better
lives. When we can accept and understand the mechanical aspects to how we experience
love, we can be in more control of these instincts and these addicting neurochemicals. If
there is real love, we will only be able to enhance it and bring it into the world fully,
when we are able to strip away the mechanical and material reality that makes up most
of it. Learning to break the brains illusions and addictions, that keep us alive, will free us
so we can live. Trying to disprove your own idea of love, has the potential of revealing
the truer nature of that love inside yourself. Honesty is a continual inner process of
challenging one’s assumptions and facing the reality of who you are as a person, and it
is not about saying what you believe to be true.

Demystifying Love: A Failed Act of Science:

Science has to sell the humanity in taking away the very things we think are our own
humanity. Most adults can understand that romantic first love, is more like a drug
addiction, with immature emotional development, making sweet beautiful lies seem like
they are real. Some people live lives chasing after that feeling of “real love”, they had
one time, and yet never again feel that “truth” in falling in love. We can use science to,
maybe one day, treat and identify these “love addictions”. No one will ever love a
person, the way they imagine their mothers loved them. Freud’s belief in an Oedipus
complex was not good science, though it was interesting thought experiment for those
that might have one, to unravel their attachments to their mother from the reality of real
relationships. Science can help push back against unhealthy forms of thinking, we often
associate with love, and help people live happier lives, in more fulfilling relationships.

Some people may think marriage is a great lie and in the future, we will evolve beyond
marriage. It is more likely we will develop a better understanding of how to have more
stable long-term relationships, that deal with the animalistic instincts and contradictory
feeling within us. Bad marriages exist, and maybe most of them are rather horrible, this
doesn’t mean marriage and love are things we need to evolve past as we go into the
future. A future with no love, no marriage, doesn’t seem very human. We can use
technology and science to find the most human ways to connect us and provide us more
rewarding lives. It can help support long standing institutions, rather than create new
social institutions from nothing. Science can’t model all the elements and variables that
form culture and society from experiments, because they can never know all the
variables to test for nor be able to isolate them all.

A Philosophy of Science

Hard science is driven by one thing, the study of cause and effect. We see a result and
we look for the cause. Primitive thinking projects magical like feelings into things, to
explain their causality. History, time, the universe, the stars, nature, have all been
things embodied with deep magical thinking, through most of human existence. Science
challenged all our presumptions and forced us to make experiments and find out what
really caused something to happen, and challenge our own deeply held emotionally
driven models of reality. What we imagine causes things, is often wrong. What we think
are connected together often have no real connection. What we think have no
connection, are deeply connected to and caused by the same thing. This is the challenge
of science. Scientific models are functional and always evolving, they are not truth, or
some certain definitive thing. We can always find deeper causes to things, and can
always make more useful models to use to better human life.

A scientific process can begin like this, you see that babies cry and when you feed them,
they stop crying. So, you make a hypothesis that babies cry because they are hungry.
You then make an experiment to test this. Now as you can obviously know, the
experiment will disprove the hypothesis, and the hypothesis will need to be modified.
Babies cry when they want something. And you can try to get more data on what babies
want, and try to design an experiment. You keep doing this over and over, until you
have lots of data, lots of failed experiments. You may reach a point where you study all
infant emotion and how babies, think and learn. You can scan their brains, and watch
them perform tasks like rats in a maze. The model you are making will slowly improve
over time, and yet may never really work. Studying physical things like rocks is much
easier. You can hypothesize that big rocks will fall as fast as small rocks, and make an
experiment. We all know those kinds of experiments. The scientific method is an
evolving and complex thing, with deep implications about how we can learn about the
world, from how we implement and develop it. Idealized perfect science, doesn’t exist,
because this a human thing, serving human purposes.

Traditional science does experiments in boxes. It isolates and analyzes variables to find
what caused what. The scientist is like god overlooking the experiment. They live in
separate realities. The idea that you can step back and observe things as an outside
observer and determine what is true, is a common misconception of the world. You can
never fully step back and observe something and see what caused what. Science is good
at studying things it can put in boxes, cut off from the rest of the world, and look down
into with a god’s eye view. It is like being up on a mountain top and looking down and
seeing things happen, and knowing objectively what caused what. You are far enough
away to not influence things, and can see how things really happen. In the real universe,
there is no gods eye view, there is no place you can step back to and get an objective
point of view on what caused what. You can’t even know the sequence of events
objectively, if you stand back far enough and view them.

Newtonian thinking was modern thinking. He invented the modern era and new kind of
thinking. You really could step back and look at the world and know how it works. A
clockwork universe, governed by rules that people could find and know, was a defining
belief of an age. They believed they could find the definitive rules and causes for
everything like a machine, and then be able to control everything in the world like a
machine. As science became a new god, it created totalitarian governments believing
they were the true heirs of science and understood the roots causes of all humanity.
Post-modernism and the failures of the past, smashed that ordered, structured, and
failing world. We didn’t want to be cogs in a vast machine, with no souls, and only
programed and conditioned by what sensory inputs we had been subjected to by
authorities. Newtonian inspired enlightenment thinking lead to totalitarianism, and a
harsh mechanical world, where we believed we could control the exact future and create
a perfect world. The industrial revolution can be seen as a spiritual process of turning
men into cogs in a vast mechanical machine, and the politics that rejected that was
more fueled by peoples discontent than any ideology. Magic and god died in the 19th
century. We found new ways of dreaming of humans as Gods capable of controlling time.

Einstein

Einstein smashed the old paradigm, and made a new one that defined the 20th century.
His theories seem so abstract as to be magic. In reality, they are just simple and direct
logic applied to reality and working out the consequences of that logic, no matter where
they may lead. You don’t often associate with relativity, in the casual sense, extreme
dedication to logic, reason, and empirical reality. He found a deeper way to explain the
fundamental roots of causality in our universe, and this upended an entire structured
and ordered sense of what was real and solid to the world. If one sees the world like

Newton, it would be really hard to fully accept modern physics. Not even Einstein himself
could accept it all, because his mind was born out of an older age of thinking. He though
followed his own inner vision and made it work out into hard science. He wanted to find
those ordered and structured rules that explained the universe, no matter how obtuse or
against common sense they may have felt.

It is important to understand his work and not avoid its fundamental ideas. Relativity
isn’t really about “relativity”. It is about Locality. If we had called it “General Locality”,
and said “everything is local”, I think there may have been some very different results in
how people integrated his ideas into popular culture. Einstein’s achievement in life was
redefining causality. He made new mathematics to describe causal relationships in
physics by creating a whole new way to conceive of how space and time work together.
It wasn’t some random relativity, with no truth, no center. The great tragedy of the 20th
century was the poor morally philosophy that people developed out their crude and poor
understandings of relativity. “Everything being relative”, moral relativity, and where
people no longer believed nor advocated in any sort of truth, eroded all of society, and
brought about conflict and societal collapse. When the foundational paradigm of an age
was disproved, it unhinged most people from reality and science.

Causality and locality are important ideas to learn from Einstein. Our schools barely
teach his root ideas; they don’t even approach them. Yet they are the most successful
modeling of reality in the history of mankind. People are afraid of looking stupid by
stepping into totally new ways of thinking and doing things. Even physicists often don’t
really understand the basics of it. The math is hard; the visualizations are easy.
Elementary school children could be taught these things, along with quantum physics. It
would be fun, and not really that hard.

Science changed after Einstein, and not all for the better. Einstein flipped the scientific
process on its head, and changed the very philosophical underpinnings that science had
been using up until that point. Einstein used experiments to prove his theory, he didn’t
use experiments to come up with his theory. He achieved what he did, by not following
the traditional process, not studying in the school’s scientists did, and not following the
things they did. He was a free thinker, and used his imagination freely. Ironically, we
crush this out of people in our education systems, and in the study of physics. Being able
to let go of the past and build a new model of what caused what, takes courage.

In some ways, he was a philosopher first and a scientist second. What he did lies outside
the realm of empirical observation and experiments. The post-modern age was born in
Einstein’s work, even if he wanted nothing to do with it. He inspired something and gave
shape to inner feelings discontented with a falsely ordered Newtonian modern world. He
is more a celebrity and a symbol than a human being at times. The world wanted to
burn, and they did a fine job of it, in the years that would follow. He even gave the
match to make the biggest “flame” of all that could burn cities to the ground in a second.
With the power to be smart that he gave us, he also helped unleash some of our
greatest stupidities.

Newton and The Ideal Observer

Causality became something different in Einstein than with Newton. The scientific
method and how the world was seen up until Einstein, was Newtonian. It was a
mechanical universe. Causality in a mechanical universe is very simple. You just observe
what did what, and make experiments to ensure that something caused something else.

You can’t assume that watching something hit something else, caused it to move. You
need to experiment, isolate all the variables and find out the truth. Everything can be
analyzed, measured, and determined, with enough study and time. Science had a good
method of working out how to deal with finding out how things work. Something is
scientific if it can be tested. Testing is where we can isolate each variable and test
variables independently, to find which one did what. Our assumptions are often wrong. If
we can step back as much as possible from an experiment, we can achieve nearly
perfect results. True objectivity in science was believed to be possible and that there is
an absolute universal truth, that we can know, through correct observation.

The outside observer has this “gods eye view” of things, and can make objective
analysis. In the case of Newtonian relativity, you could be on a moving train and throw a
ball to someone, if you observed the motion of this ball moving from the perspective of
the train it would be very different than its motion relative to the train track. From the
prospective inside an idealized smoothly moving fast, but non-accelerating train, you
would have no idea if you moving or not, so the balls movement to you would seem
true. A distant outside observer could look down, and see all the different ways it could
be observed. Newtonian Relativity was showing a different way to see causality. Your
frame of reference would define your perspective of causality, and only when you could
step out of the system, could you see the real causes of things. Inertia made more sense
mathematically, though even in its simplest form, is still hard for most people to
understand. He gave mathematical tools so a person could transform their perspective of
something into a truer one. The ball is at rest, relative the train, and moving relative to
a fixed position on the earth.

You can basically understand the contrast of modernism vs post modernism, with just
this one idea, and its fall. A mechanical universe was a beautiful lie, that worked so well,
for so many things. The gods eye can reveal so many truths, for all the things you can

put in a box or make into a simple machine. It can create the wonders of an industrial
age. You can at a personal and emotional level feel how such thinking would constrict
and choke people, who didn’t fit into that mechanical model. There is something missing.
You need to really step back and think about this box, and who is doing the observing.
There is always an observer, there is always a person inside that experiment. The “box”
is never really solid and clearly defined.

The most disturbing things from the conclusion of Einstein’s work, was that there was no
clear causality and no clear objective point of view. There was no stepping outside the
box and getting a god’s eye view of things. There are many ways to understand this, and
come to this conclusion in physics, in the study of the small, the very big, and even in
mathematics itself. We can’t ever truly take a god’s eye view of the world and know
clearly how it works. Einstein wasn’t wholly stepping outside of Newton’s classic
mechanical world, he however opened a door to undermine the conception that things
can be truly objectively observed, and used a different way to do science, that didn’t
wholly rely on pure empirical experiments and observation to develop a theory. There is
a kind of magic in his ideas, and to understand his view of time, takes some serious
leaps of thinking and imagination that most people have not. General relativity doesn’t
remove objective time, it merely makes objective observing it nearly impossible, since
we can’t go observing the universe from 20 random points spread through the universe
and confirm what we see. The speed of light changes things. Causality itself gained a
speed, and became bound in time, in a defined way, where it hadn’t been before.

Math and Science

It isn’t obvious that the world can be described with math, and actually goes against any
basic common sense. Connecting all the dots in numbers into abstract theories, takes
very specialized, trained, and focused minds. If you could lay out basic math, that could
explain the underlying order of the world, that math would almost be magical, and seem
to come from a god or another universe. Making solid models of the universe to describe
reality takes more than just a traditional procedural approach to science.

Newton really ushered in the era of truly connecting science and math together. The
great astronomers before him had started this process. He really brought down into the
earth and made it a full viable movement. Physics and math, became a bound and
inseparable relationship. Though beneath this apparent super objectivity lies a far more
human story. Math is far more human and nearly magical, than people like to imagine.
Most of math that we have now is based on magic. We don’t really even know what
numbers are other than that it is a notation system that really works well.

Traditional science and math work together like this,
1. if we do enough observations and experiments, we start to get a lot of numbers,
that seem to really connect and relate at a deeper level than just causality.
2. We can start to make basic mathematical models that can explain how things
work.

People that are good at math traditionally are not the types to go out and about
exploring the world. Scientists and mathematicians are not of the same species of
intellectual. The process of making good math from science, takes very different kinds of

thinking than the kind used to go do science. It becomes a sort of chicken and egg
argument. Science is grounding and more connected to reality, than the math. More
people can do good science than good math. Math creates rarer super freaks. It creates
supermen. A person obsessed with the nature of reason and the inner processes of
thought, tend to end up with very strong minds or insane. The fact that we can describe
physics with math, seems only now obvious. If you study math your whole life and
deeply think about how to explain things with math, then you will be biased to believe in
mathematical rules more than reality itself. There are scientists that will say their model
is true, even when it doesn’t match the world at all. This dedication to mental delusions
can create religious zealots, masterpieces of philosophy and even scientific theories that
change the world. It can also just lead to being an idiot with a lot of brain power, and no
real connections to the world.

This is summed up in two different types of logic. Science used a new type of logic called
induction, to ignite the scientific revolution. The old mathematical form of reasoning,
deduction, had been around for thousands of years. Math had developed through the
eons, while science never really developed in any sort of steady manner ever, until the
17th century. Deduction and induction use logic in completely opposite directions. Over
centuries they have learned how to get along, and the separations are not so obvious in
our modern world. In the 17th - 19th century, they were far more separated and arguing
about truth. Math people are better at deductive logic, and science people are better at
inductive logic. Rare people like Newton were masters of both. He could do all the
scientific observations, and make a mathematical model. Getting different kinds of
thinking and different processes working together well, lies at the heart of how science
has improved. It isn’t just about logic and the meaning of truth. It is different groups of
smart people learning to get along and agree on a shared process, to create collective
results, that made science evolve and be so awesome. At a basic level, it was like two
religions arguing over the nature of god, and it is super ridiculous. “God comes from

above and orders the world”, “god comes from inside, and we can know his will through
reflection and reason”. Great theological battles evolved into scientific battles, and the
underlying issues and feelings where still the same. The mathematician mind had to
learn to connect their ideas to the world directly, and the scientific mind had to learn to
describe their observations in math. They both then could begin to work together, with a
shared language of Science.

Now all people are naturally from birth a “rationalist” or an “empiricist”. It is just the
direction your sense of logic, order and identity move towards. One moves inwards and
the other outwards, and both are still logic and do mostly the same things. It is
something ingrained in the very cognitive functions of how your brain works and thinks.
This is not some abstract impersonal thing. Different people in the sciences
fundamentally think differently and have massive clashes of differing ways of ordering
reality. These arguments are deeply emotional. Most people have inclinations to be
attracted to different sorts of methods of doing things, over others. They will be more
comfortable sorting things into different categories than other ways of sorting things.
There isn’t exactly a wrong or right way, there is just the reality that people come into
the sciences with different inclinations towards different methodologies. One doesn’t
merely adopt a philosophical framework, one is born with one you are more inclined to
adopt; then you go out and fill it up with things that compliment or clash with it, and try
to work it all out to be consistent with your own self and mind.

These two schools of thought Empiricisms and Rationalism are awesome, and both if left
alone to themselves, lead to some pretty insane conclusions. Humanity needs both to
work together, and they do. I don’t want to get into this nutty and insane conflict. It is
large obnoxious egos attacking each other for centuries. They used two different kinds of
logic, induction and deduction. Empiricism won for a long time, and ordered the entire

modern world into boxes and manageable systems. It defines economics and
government to this day. The 20th century is more a story of rationalisms return.
Rationalism is really good with computers, and Newton’s greatest rivals work is almost
like a guidebook to computers. Rationalism from its first great masters had computers
on their wacky heads centuries before their invention. Descartes had robots, and Leibniz
actually talked about thinking machines. Newton ran the treasury of England, and spent
most of his life trying to make gold.

Empiricism

A basic way to understand this is that empiricists love to go explore the world and look
at things. They can pick up rocks and they are actually fascinated by different kinds of
rocks, and not just because one is pretty or not. They are curious about the world.
Empiricism at its most basic level is about looking at the world and putting different
things in different boxes. They believe that what we see and feel with our senses is what
is most true. The logic of putting things in boxes is defined by things intentions and
purpose. There is a softness contained within the logical structure that favors things that
are useful to people, and in doing practical things. Boxes just have to be functional and
be useful, rather than perfect.

For an empiricist, identity is made from your life experiences and the things their senses
have felt. Your identity is created out of the environment you live in, and it will also
create an attachment to that arbitrary reality, which is you. Your very sense of self is
created from your connection and experience of reality. The only thing you can ever
know, is what your senses feel. Your mind organizes those senses into a mental
mapping of reality, and this becomes you. The logic of empiricism is to apply logic to this
way of being attached to your senses as reality. Empiricism is not just some cold form of

logic being imposed on the sensory reality we live in. It arises out of deeper softer more
complex emotions of self, intentionality and compassion. You can find these sorts of
feelings in eastern thinking. The underlying thinking of empiricism is very similar to
eastern spirituality. It is call phenomenology or in some ways teleology, in formal
philosophy.

It then develops around it a more externalized logic and structure. The empiricist uses a
kind of logic that organizes the world that we see. An objective logical order on the world
manifests out from their own emotions and feelings. The literal making of a city into
grids with square buildings, and straight roads, is a direct manifestation of this logic. You
can see that this kind of logic is very different than a rationalist mathematician. It wants
to know what is what, and where things will be in the future. It wants to make a
predictable and safe world. The logic of kings and leaders is made into science itself, so
that we can rule not only people, we can rule the very reality of the universe. This
begins with a process of reasoning, and working it out slowly through time. Inner warm
fuzzies can manifest themselves into an ordered world that protects us as individuals
and organizes us together as a unified group. We create a logical and structured future
through empirical logic, with clear chains of command and order.

The rules that one develops to define what a box is, is most of the knowledge of science.
We classify all living things in a massive hierarchy of rules. You can’t be a mammal if
you lay eggs. A mammal is defined by a set of rules. Kangaroos look like mammals, but
don’t fit all the rules, so have to be put in a new box. Science is about rules you impose
on nature: boxes and categories. You write down what you see, record numbers, and
collect as much objective data as you can. These boxes are not real, they are arbitrary
categories that we make, based on how we feel, and what feels like a group, and not a
group. This feeling is organized into a set of rules. The actual rules can be changed, if

our sense of purpose and identity in those categories change. We could base those
categories on entirely different feelings, and still have just as solid a system. We could
organize life around their degrees of domestication and usefulness to us. Their
relationship and connection to humanity would shape a classification system.

The world around us is what is most real. All knowledge comes from experience and the
world we see around us. Science is naturally very similar to government and
bureaucracy. The rules and laws are arbitrary. We judge the quality of a government by
how effective it is at controlling things. We judge the boxes we use to organize things,
by how useful they are to us as human beings. Words that we use to label things, are
based on human emotion and feelings. An object has a word attached to it based on its
usefulness to us. A planet with no life on it, barely has anything to label with words,
unless it something we can modify to create something with that is useful. Iron ore
makes iron, and iron is what we make things out of that are very strong and useful to
us. If you shove a pen into an apple, it is just an apple with a pen shoved into it, and not
a new thing, with a new word, because that thing in of itself has no useful function,
unless we want to make apple-pens into a concept to describe categorical silliness.
Science has to label everything, even if its relationship to humanity is distant, and there
is no clear usefulness in it. Empiricisms logic can push language, labels, and boxes onto
all of reality, that is even outside of what we can readily feel and connect to. It is the
process of ordering reality that we can’t control yet, so we can make it useful for human
use and feelings, eventually.

Empiricism doesn’t lead to truth. It leads to effective systems for managing reality. If it
works 95% of the time, that can be good enough to call “true”. If we can know when it
will fail 5% of the time clearly, then we can simply not use that system for those 5% of
the time situations. Scientific laws are valid only for certain things, and can’t readily be

expanded to everything. You can’t use Newtonian mechanics to explain the universe.
This way of thinking focuses on what it can do, and tries to slowly expand its power to
include more and more things. Newtonian principles were slowly applied to more and
more things, that it could work on, and it didn’t always succeed. It couldn’t explain race,
good government, mercuries orbit, particle wave duality, ether, religion, how women
think, and so on. The world itself was transformed by this expansion of power. We could
use basic rules and ideas and apply them into more and more aspects of life. We could
harness power, and use it to control the very world we live in. It also reaches a limit,
and then we need to make math and theories for that other “5%”.

We base scientific laws as being laws based on their usefulness, not their truth. This
applies to things like quantum mechanics which are pure empiricism, and have little
correlation to reality and truth, these laws however do a great job calculating stuff in a
narrow range of things. It isn’t that laws are just useful; it is that they are easier to do
the math with, and thus more useable and teachable. Complex math, that is hard, and
more accurate, is less useful than approximate math that is easier. Any sort of difficult
or hard math, to an empiricist, unless absolutely necessary will not be favored over
easier math, that works good enough. General relativity is more “true”, and it has
horribly difficult math to use, and thus more empirically minded people rejected it based
on utility and personal feelings. This is completely rational and appropriate.

When we tried to apply Newtonian thinking into people, this leads to management
theories, finance, and economics. Human beings became parts in massive theoretical
machines. We studied how to manage people like things, and integrate them into the
vast machinery of the modern world that science had built. Industrial and office workers
toiling away in repetitive jobs, became the very image of industry and progress. We
developed entire schools of thought where could manage society towards a better

future. Government and science together, seemed poised to solve all the problems of
life. All those emotions people were feeling, shaped what was to come. The wars, the
conflicts and deaths on scales never seen in world history would frame the greatest age
in human advancement ever seen. All that death and wonder was born from power,
science, and a quest to order the world. We still think with Newtonian like ideas in
economics, politics, government, finance, and it still leads to disasters. People think they
can understand the clockwork machinery and manage it, with simple and easy to use
math. Science wedded to government is always bound up in imposing an ordered
structure onto reality that makes it more usable to humanity as a collective entity.
Science and politics, bound together, is idealized totalitarianism. “Let’s save the world
with….Science!”.

Rationalism

Math is a bit different than science. It is inwardly turned, and much more personal to the
person, that develops and uses it. A mathematician is a very weird sort of man. Nearly
all mathematicians are men. Great women in math are mostly all in computer science,
and there are some amazing ones in that field. Science is much more appealing to
women, than math, historically. Math requires a level of personal sacrifice, that few
people can make. You have to live inside your head, and disconnect from the world, and
at some level be completely oblivious to people and life. I don’t suggest becoming a
theoretical mathematician. They take something they see, and apply logic to it. They
take things to extreme logical ends, and go as far as they possibly can, down into the
tiniest detail. They can argue over the grammar of a sentence for 3 years. They care
about what things mean, and how you express them. They are marveled by the inner
power of the mind. “I think therefore I am”.

Science had to use induction, and by freeing itself from deduction, did the world a great
service. It required people observe the world, and collect data, first! Too much of history
is philosophers thinking they have discovered an eternal truth, and revealing it to the
world. Rationalism descends into religion and mystical thinking readily. They believe in
things that can’t be seen. They develop elaborate models of alternate realities that can
never be observed. Science liberated people from this insanity. It made things solid, real
and empirical. It made it possible for ideas to more directly rule the world. Rationalists
make religions, empiricists make governments. The rationalist’s minds digs into the
origins of everything and into the very identity of creation, while the empiricists tries to
order and create a future.

The feeling of being a rationalist is rather mystical. It is not just following logical
thoughts to their natural conclusions. On the outside a rationalist uses a form of logic
that exposes interrelated truths contained in the things we know. It unpacks things and
takes them to their logical ends. Logic becomes a chain of connections, and the
rationalist searches for chains within things that can link back towards deeper truths.
Most of the process produces junk thinking. Trains of thought that lead to nowhere have
to be abandoned and new paths taken up. Digging into reality in search of its underlying
logic and rules takes time and most of the work can’t be shared with others. Tight and
true connections have to be found, and not just generalities. They don’t want things to
be just functional and useful, they want absolute concepts that work all the time. They
dig backwards to root causes, beyond what can even be observed. They really think
about the beginning, the very first thing. They want to just be able to unravel life with a
few hacks, and find root ideas that can create all the things we see around us.

The feeling of finding something beautiful is exhilarating. It is like looking for diamonds
in your own mind. In the darkness, there are moments of sharp and clear insight that

make it possible to see new things. Digging into one’s own thinking to find the root of
who you are and the meaning of life, are fulfilling things to a rationalist. They enjoy their
own thoughts more than others thoughts. They love to solve puzzles and explore the
mysteries of things beyond what we can touch. Finding out how to play the world as a
grand game, can also be a great pleasure. To really understand deduction and
rationalism, you need to understand its emotional reality. This is not a warm and fuzzy
way of thinking at any level. Pure rationalist minds don’t like sentimental closeness and
warmth from people. They can be very social and deeply connected to people though.
They are in many ways more social than empiricists. They treasure their personal
relationships far more, and are deeply influenced by those around them. Nearly all
rationalists in history have been very devout religious people, above and beyond the
standards of their own time. Math and sainthood, have a bit of a relationship.

Rationalism has the power to create knowledge from nothing. You take a set of basic
things and begin playing around with them. If get the right set of things to play with,
one can begin to see a puzzle to find how they connect and interrelate. The rationalist
mind loves puzzles, and in puzzles they can find simple connections and sequences
between things. When you take that set of things, you can logically explore what the
causal relationships are between things. You can by just using logic deduce certain
relationships must be true and not others. This can produce amazing results and also
delude people into thinking this is how all truth is found. Deductions can also just be
guesses, that a person then works out and builds complex systems around. If the
system ends up working well, based on their basic deductions, they can be very happy.
They often don’t want to test their systems in the world, nor share their ideas, unless
they are certain they work. It is embarrassing for their minds to be exposed and to have
logic errors in them.

Modern Science and The Old

Science respects what has worked before. If there is a new theory, science has a rule,
Occam’s razor, to respect older theories more than newer theories. We often learn this in
a different way in school, we are told to take the simplest theory that works, and not
more complex ones. “Simpler” means respecting older models, and building on those.
This inductive process doesn’t care about truth. It just wants something that works, and
it is much simpler to just make small modifications and evolve a system, than overthrow
it with a new one. If it works good enough, then it slowly becomes a scientific law. No
scientific law works all the time, just enough, that it is has a practical usefulness for
doing day to day things. This creates a bias towards more grounded and real thinking,
and that is a good thing, until it isn’t. Science must always begin from a traditional
method and work up a large collection of models and data. It will always reach a point
that it can’t go past, where science stalls, and can’t find a way out. This is when you
need to invert the whole method. You need to make a theory, predict data, design an
experiment to get the data you want, then develop new questions to ask about the
world, and remake all the observed data of history.

When you need to create a completely new paradigm, it is very hard to smash the old
one and build another. Science loves to gradually build on the discoveries from before. It
is a slow process, that is not about finding the truth. It is a process of testing things,
that needs to be humble, gradual, and very skeptical of individual human reason.
Empirical science is a very collective and process oriented way of doing things. This way
of doing things creates gradual and steady growth, until it hits something, that its path
simply can’t understand, and can’t process. All systems fail. Empirical science by its very
nature will always fail at critical points, and never be able to make complete models, or
fully function ones. The scientific method itself is a process that can’t always work, due

to its need to make a system that can order, predict and control the world. At a certain
point things, just don’t fit into ordered logical boxes perfectly. This is because causation
itself within induction is probabilistic and thus all formal systems must be defined by
probability and not “truths”. Empiricism predicts the future, and the future is not a set
and determined thing governed by clockwork rules.

Flipping the scientific method on its head seems really cool, it however makes for some
insane science. People become free to just imagine whatever they want, devoid of any
actual data or observation. Models become reality more than data. Computer made
models that say something is true, become truth, even when the models don’t work.
Math can be used to self-rationalize whatever a person wants to believe, and when put
into a computer can make them seem devoid of personal bias. Math is just a tool, and
good math, doesn’t prove a good idea. All good ideas have good math, not all good math
has good ideas. If great math doesn’t back up experiments that come from flipping the
process, then it will certainly fail.

New paradigms are made by rare individuals. Science doesn’t like overthrowing its Gods.
Many scientists still follow Newton, and just think of Einstein as a fringe thing for exotic
stuff. Other scientists follow Einstein like a god, and justify everything they do, based on
his thinking. Even when they say he was wrong on certain things, due to being a mortal
man, they worship an overall idea and approach to science. Einstein’s idol was Michael
Faraday and he was the greatest scientific mind of the 19th century, whose vision of
physics laid the ground work for Einstein’s great works. Faraday did this nutty thing
where he built experiments, to generate the data he wanted them to generate. He first
came up with a theory, then the data it would create, then an experiment to generate
that data. When the experiment didn’t give the data he wanted, he changed the
experiment until it did. He approached science like a crack-pot, and created a whole new

paradigm to see science from. The scientific method done in reverse can create
paradigm shifts. The focus of science shifts from creating great experiments that can be
deeply tested, to creating outlandish models that experiments can readily falsify.

Modern science at that time, if it had steadily followed Newtonian science, would never
have made the achievements Faraday did. He had a strong inner vision and belief, and
he manifested it into reality, and proved it through experiments that actually worked.
Though this methodology doesn’t work for most everyday science. He also couldn’t
create the full mathematical description of his work, that Maxwell created for him.
History seems to remember Maxwell more than the crackpot inventor of a new paradigm
of thinking.

A Different Method of Science Explained.

When science reaches places where it can’t put things in a box, then it needs to use a
different scientific method to explore things. This is why social sciences and psychology
rarely produce any useful or real science. You can’t really study people in a box. We can
study babies and little kids in a box, because they are mentally not connected to much
of the world yet. We can study how human minds work when we strap that brain down
into an actual “box” that scans their brain patterns as they think. Cognitive neuroscience
can do good science, because it can isolate the brains functions to some degree. The
problem with most all social sciences is that the scientists will always be in the box with
those they observe, and we can’t really cut people out from the world in a box, and not
expect their behavior to change.

You have to make the person in the box a more consistent and knowable thing, if we are
inside the box with the universe. Rationalism is a good way to come to conclusions when
you are in the box with the universe. The rationalist begins by believing that your mind
and you, are the only certain thing. So, it is very good at cleaning up this mind to do
amazing things. Rationalists get good at math, and having clear consistent thinking
internally. They dig into themselves to find the root causality of their own thinking.
When we do science, we need to dig into our own reasons that we are doing science and
the real goals we have. When we do social sciences, people often hide their real thinking
and pretend to be doing objective science in a box. Current social sciences, in my age,
are deeply connected to government power and promoting totalitarian government
systems to control and manage people. Since the feed the vanity of the state, they get
generous funding, with little to no valid results.

Rationalism can do something empiricism can’t and at times it is very important for its
mysticism to be let out. Rationalism requires a bit of magic to work. When Einstein as a
child realized that light couldn’t double in speed, it wasn’t based on empirical
observation. He just felt it to be true as a kind of basic logic. This deductive insight, he
would then later work out to show how light really worked. It was that feeling deep
inside him, that he worked and explained the nature of universe with, and not years of
focused study of facts and figures on planets and stars. If we look at the universe and its
basic properties we have to consider what caused what, and the fundamental levels of
reality. With just thought experiments fundamental features of the universe can be
guessed to exist, and then actually found. With just a few pieces of information, a
rationalist mind can dig into the logical structure of things and deduce truths. A modern
rationalist though has to take their idea and go test it and make sure it can be tested. If
it can’t be tested, then the idea is nonsense, no matter how beautiful the idea. They
have to have the courage to show their beautiful ideas to others, and do their best to
prove them wrong.

A SIDE NOTE: RATIONALIST MATERIALISM

There is a modern school of rationalist thinking, called Rationalist Materialism I want to
comment on. I don’t endorse it wholly, nor completely reject it. They are fundamentalist
atheists. It is a confusing school of influential thinking that should be explained. This
explanation can help illuminate some very deep ideas about different ways to approach
science. Since I am by nature a rationalist, I do care about the nuances. The differing
schools of thought that a rationalist can hold don’t all get along. If you believe A caused
B or B caused A, and A and B are important things, then 2 schools of thinking, would
have deeply divergent views. At the heart of rationalism is dualism and Plato’s allegory
of the cave. This story covers pretty much all there is to know about rationalism. Plato’s
great classic “The Republic” is the story of what one should do, if you do leave the cave
and come inside it. This all may seem very abstract and not relevant to one’s immediate
life. There are people living their lives by these ideas, and some of them can have
considerable influence. If we take Plato’s cave and see this as literally real, and not a
metaphor, this can create 2 very different schools of thought. In a basic rationalist way,
we imagine that truth and reality are outside the cave.

In a modern rationalist materialist view, we would describe that reality as what is real.
Science then becomes the real-life process of revealing truth into reality and stripping
back human perceptions of shadows. The shadows are our human limitations and
cognitive bias that we evolved to perceive reality, and with deeper study and science we
can help peel back these mental delusions and more closely arrive at truth. We project
by human nature magic into the shadows in the wall to explain how they form and exist.
Rationalists by nature are magical thinkers, that need to solve the problem of this kind
of thinking and minimize it. Science can be one way to minimize it, by creating a system

that falsifies their magical models and ideas. Rationalist scientific processes are driven
by a Karl Popper style method. They can go out of their way to disprove their most
cherished ideas, as a way to push forward science. You need to keep alive the magic and
vitality in Rationalism and temper it with deep internal skepticism and fearlessness in
exposing themselves as being wrong. Rationalists are very proud of their own thinking
and exposing it to deep ridicule and the highest chance of being shown to be illogical,
takes a kind of moral character.

Science steps outside the cave, and sees reality and brings those truths back to the
cave. Anything that fights against this truth and revelation is a negative force that must
be organized against and rooted out. The process of science is to liberate people from
the bondage of perceiving reality as shadows, and help them through reason, education,
and social institutions live a more real and healthy life. The true world creates our world
of shadows and those that perceive that true world, should rule and organize the world
of shadows. They believe that they can determine values, morality and politics, from
truth outside the cave. It is by nature an idealistic utopian authoritarian philosophy.
Plato’s Republic is a guide to building a utopian society, and thus is a guidebook to
authoritarianism. A small group of people will determine through science what is morally
true and then impose that on an unenlightened society. If they do the scientific method
correctly and there is actual objectively true morality that can be imposed on a society,
then there is in theory the potential to create an ideal and better world. Objective
external moral structures bound into and defined by deductive logic and reason, is an
enduring quality to rationalist thought. This morality would arise from an understanding
of the material nature of human consciousness and social evolution. We would study,
brains, DNA, and computer models to determine social values.

This is a powerful set of ideas, and deeply appealing to many rationalist minded people’s
idealism and internal self-belief in their own intelligence over that of other people. It is
not a theory driven by Marxism, Collectivism, or Identity politics. It is in many ways a
right wing theocratic ideology, with no God. They are seeking to create a new social
order and religion to order society. In order for their ideas to work, they need to
recognize a need to separate their ideology from politics and to not have a state ruled by
their atheist religion. If they seek no government power, and only try to create a noncentralized religion based on voluntary interactions, and increasing the quality of life for
people based on truths revealed in Science about human nature, then their movement
can be very successful and embraced by many. Atheism in of itself is no threat to
anyone, except those that wish to impose their beliefs on others through political and
military power. It is a new secular religion, that won’t be going away anytime soon, due
to its appeals to innate human nature found in more idealistic rationalist minds. This way
of thinking can discipline people away from useless magical thinking that their minds can
generate as natural garbage thoughts we all have. They first will have to create a moral
character in their adherents in how deeply they can challenge their own thinking and
expose it to the harshest tests of falsification. That is an intrinsic moral element
necessary for modern materialistic rationalist new athiests.

The other way of seeing Plato’s cave isn’t not a movement with a clear name yet. They
see that the shadows on the wall create the “truth” outside the cave. They are also
materialists, since pure rationalism without an appeal to the real world is not a
functioning form of ideology anymore. Kant and Jung are sort of the underpinning
