it, will stay the same width. As it approaches the speed of light, it flattens towards
nothing. This seems really weird to see from earth, to see a thing with a normal shape
flatten because it is moving so much faster relative to us, this though makes sense when
one considers the way time alters space around that rocket.

From an outside perspective think of it like this. You see 1 meter of space, and the
rocket sees 2 meters of space, on each side of it. As the speed increases the rocket sees
more and more space, and from the outside, you see the same amount of space, and
less and less rocket. It is like a line is stretching in, instead of out. The space stretches

the ship doesn’t and we see the same amount of space, and we see the new ratio of
space and time. The rocket itself is creating gravity. It is not virtual gravity, it is real
gravity. Any acceleration pushing on you like an elevator going up, a rocket launching
up, or a rocket accelerating forever, are creating real gravity, described with the same
math as the one we use to describe gravity around planets. This equivalence is what
creates general relativity.

Trying to go faster than speed of light is just like making black holes. You can think of
the black hole event horizon forming into being behind you, as you accelerate to faster
and faster speeds approaching the speed of light. “Behind” this 8g rocket is not different
gravitationally to “below” you as you stand on the earth, except for the rocket has 8Gs,
and the Earth 1G. With stars, the denser the star gets, the deeper its dimple into the
universe becomes, and this is the same with how fast any object accelerates to relative
to the rest of the universe. Space is forming around the ship, relative to the universe,
and eventually all that space will consume that ship, and separate it from the rest of the
universe. From the outside, there will be a bending of a small region of space and rocket
flatting out to nothing. These are different perspectives of the same thing. That extra
space being created is “time”. And when that “time kind of space” overwhelms the ship,
it enters into a new time frame separate from others.

From the rockets perspective, the rest of the universe is squishing into nothing. The
faster it gets, the more things it is moving away from squish towards smaller and
smaller sizes. If it reached light speed, things would squish out of existence for
everything but the rocket. If you see this just from a rockets perspective, the universe
begins to shrink to thinner and thinner lengths, the faster you go, and it takes more and
more energy for each bit of the universe to get smaller, and more energy to escape from
it. For the rocket space around the craft is stretching. It is not harder to go faster, if a

rocket is accelerating towards light speed, the “people” inside will still feel 8Gs of
acceleration.

A rocket could accelerate at 8g forever, and experience 8g acceleration forever if it had
the energy to do so, and not be affected in its acceleration at all by how close it is to
light speed, relative to the rest of the universe. The rocket experiences more space, and
simply is moving through more and more space the faster it goes. Space itself is
increasing, from the perspective of the outside observer. The reason it gets flatter and
flatter to the outside observer is because there is more and more space there. It is
seeing an object relative to its distortion of space-time. You are in a sense observing
space-time and the object being represented together. The rocket hasn’t squished, only
your perception of the space around it has increased. If that rocket where in theory to
go over light-speed, it wouldn’t become infinitely massive or energetic, it would simply
leave the universe we live in. There would be more space time around it, than light could
escape from, and reach us. It would have to create its own independent space-time from
our own. It would move out of any possible influence on us, and cease to exist as a thing
we could ever observe. It would cross an event-horizon, like a black hole, and its future
would split with ours. Acceleration and speeding away from a thing is altering the very
future and what can cause what to do what. It would create so much space between
itself and the rest of the universe that light itself couldn’t travel across all the space that
came into being.

As you approach the speed light everything behind you will start to fade to black and
become vastly more distant, with more and “space” to travel through. Only the
destination you are speeding towards will be clear. Eventually all the blackness from
behind will come around, and slowly shrink the forward view of the universe. At light
speed the universe will become black and the last dot of light that you are moving

towards will be closed off with the blackness of space, as you enter into your own
universe. Your created a new time frame by accelerating. You literally generated new
time, and it surrounded you. All acceleration is a change in time, and time from a
deeper more fundamental understanding of it as a physical thing, that you can describe
objectively.

General Relativity and Black Holes

A black hole is like one of those dents in a balloon or a mattress, that goes vertically
down really far. That curve downwards is expressed in time dilation. The deeper into the
hole the tinier changes in distance can have greater differences in time, which just
means more intense acceleration the closer you get. This warping can look like some
bottomless pit falling out of space. Visualizing the experience of going through a black
hole is not much different than approaching the speed of light for an accelerating object.
Approaching an event horizon is approaching a point where the entire universe will cease
to exist for anything crossing over an event horizon, at a simple level it is akin to moving
into another universe, with different space-time.

To the observer approaching a black hole, there is no steep indent in space-time. The
more you are on a sloped space-time, the more space you will observe. There will simply
be more space on the side of you away from the event horizon. The event horizon will
become more and more the shortest distance to you, and the points away from the black
hole behind you will have more and more space growing behind them. You will simply
experience more space, which is a representation of the curvature of time. Like any
large gravitational object there is more space on the side of you that is opposite the
object. Space is “expanding” through you in a sense. Where space is the smallest and

time moving the slowest is pointed straight at the center of gravity of a massive
gravitational object like a planet or sun.

Gravity is created by differentials in time on each side of an object, and these
differentials in time are expressed in a shifting of the curvature of space. The curve of
space is just a bit more space on one side a bit less space on the other. This difference
in space between two sides of an object can be measured with two highly accurate
clocks. If one clock is pointed towards a black hole and the other pointed away on the
other side of an object, the closer they get to the black hole, the greater the difference
in time between those two clocks, and this will directly create a distortion in the
perception of the amount of space.

Now let’s imagine you are on the surface of the Earth, and that the surface of the Earth,
wraps up and around you, so that you can see the other side of the planet, directly
above you. It would be like being on the inside surface of an empty ball, where
everything on the outside would be mirrored on the inside. You would be able to see the
entire surface of the Earth by just looking in every direction up and around you. In many
ways, this is what it is like to cross over an event horizon. The surface of one world
comes to envelope you, and encase you in a new enclosed universe of only itself. The
more you approach the event horizon the more space from the black hole will surround
and consume you. You can imagine the gradual step by step transition from a positively
curved round planet, slowly bending itself into a new curve around you. You are standing
on top of a turned over bowl, the bowl slowly flattens, and then eventually the edges of
bowl slowly rise up around you. They eventually begin to form a sphere above you, with
circle that forms above you, that gets smaller and smaller as the top of the sphere closes
of above you like the iris of a camera shutter.

That last little window of a circle that leads out of this negative sphere, is the direction
one would have to go to move back into the real universe. Once that window closes, it
can never be opened again. This curving is caused by massive amounts of space
between you and the rest of the universe, the closer to a black hole you get. You will see
the literal event horizon rise up around you as you approach it, and it will eventually
surround you completely. In terms of crossing the event horizon, all you experience is
just more and more space. There becomes this massive separation between you and the
universe that you will see as actually space. That black hole is a near infinitely deep hole
and when you are “standing” deep on the surface of the steep hole, you see only more
flat space and not deeply curved space. The universe outside of you, is what you see
curve.

In a sense, space is expanding through you. As space moves in one direction it is
grows in the direction it moves towards. These tiny differences in spaces size as it moves
in certain directions, is described by time. As space moves in any direction it expands,
and thus the whole universe expands as a product of this spatial expansion that is
caused by time itself. The expansion of the universe is a product of time, and time itself
is this very expansion of space in the direction it moves. It is a slight and tiny force, that
with enough of it adds up into something significant. Nothing can block time itself.

Now it is time to cross that event Horizon.

Crossing an Event Horizon into A New “Universe”

As the last bit of the old universe closes off above you, and you make your final decent
into a black hole, you will become aware of the “singularity”. When you cross through

the black holes event horizon you will be at the center of a massive sphere, with its walls
at large distances from you. The walls are the singularity. Inside a black hole the
singularity is not experienced as a singular point, it is seen as the entire inside surface of
sphere. The event horizon is the exact center of that sphere. There is no space and no
direction you can point that leads out of a black hole. Vast amounts of space exist
between you and the old universe, such that space itself is a wall between you and the
old, and all you can see is just empty space. In a black hole, all futures and all directions
points towards the singularity, thus the in any direction you can spin or orient yourself is
the black holes singularity. If you move in any direction, you move closer to the
singularity. You can almost imagine the surface of the singularity and the surface of the
event horizon as very similar the event horizon rises up around you to form a sphere of
space and time, and when it closes the inside of that surface is seen as the singularity
itself.

Now let’s imagine you orbited the event horizon before crossing into it. Instead of just
falling through the event horizon, you accelerated up to 99% the speed of light, with an
orbit just above the event horizon of a black hole. This would be the only way to sort of
stand still when you cross a black hole’s event horizon. Now a magic rocket could be half
across an event horizon and half outside of it, in orbit at 99% the speed of light. Rather
than be like a ball spinning around a roulette table, the very surface of the roulette
wheel would be curving up and closing above the spinning ball. I am not sure the exact
geometry of this or how rocket can be half in and half out. The gradation between the
event horizon is a smooth surface of a lot space.

Now the event horizon may very well be a point in space and time, where the difference
on side to the other side is so different in time, that even at the quantum level of a
particle that the differences in time between each side of the particle are so extreme as

to rip that particle in half. If you imagine a 1-km-long-bar of 10-meter-thick steel going
towards a black hole, it would certainly stretch into a thin wire way before it reached the
event horizon. Difference in time will cause stretching at the most extreme forms of
dilation, it would cause noticeable stretching even at the level of an atom. This is
unknown to me at the moment, how steep an event horizon is, and the crossing over is
more of a visual metaphor, than something a person could actually do.

Crossing the Singularity

The singularity is around you in every direction. It is almost like quantum physics is
made real in the large scales of the universe. The expression of a super dense singularity
is experienced as a spread-out form in every direction you can see. You are like on the
inside of a quantum universe. This surface won’t be uniform, and not all directions will
be the same. The singularity will have variations across its surface. This is inherent due
to the fundamental laws of quantum physics. There is an inherent uncertainty as to the
state, momentum and position of anything you observe. Quantum uncertainty is an
actual feature of quantum physics and not just a problem with how we observe things.

At the deepest levels of our universe, at its smallest scale, things have randomness. This
randomness is one of the great mysteries of all science, social sciences, philosophy and
religion. At some level, the universe just flips a coin which direction it is going to go. Up
or down, and it is completely random and unpredictable. Tiny variations in randomness
can create tiny unique and fleeting structures. If we take empty space, at any point in
empty space, anything can appear in that space, with some probability. I exist to some
degree in every point in the universe. There is no such thing as an empty box. There is
no such thing as zero. If you ask how many apples there are in an empty box, that is
perfectly isolated from everything in the universe, the number is never zero. There is

always a certain possibility of an apple being in that box. It is number so small as to be
incomprehensible. General relativity can be described as the geometry of space time. It
uses the actually shapes and curves of lines in geometry to describe space and time. At
the smallest quantum level these sorts of generalized geometries simply can’t model
uncertainty. We would be looking at quantum uncertainty itself made massive in scale,
possibly. Does geometry create quantum uncertainty?

The challenge in understanding what it is to hit the surface of that singularity is to
understand the geometry of quantum physics. That surface will have a structure and
patterns in it. Those patterns will define what the shape of quantum physics underlying
reality really are, rather than just descriptions that work perfectly. Space and time are
emergent prosperities of the geometry of space and time at its fundamental root level.
Quantum physics describes how that quantum space time alters systems through time.
Matter rests on space and time, and at the tiniest levels it doesn’t move like things do at
the big. Time is truly a defined and specific structure at this level, that can never be
observed, except inside a black hole.

Combining General Relativity and Quantum Physics

Fine Tuning

Physics has a puzzle to solve. It seems the universe can’t have its rules if there is just
one universe, and there not be a god. Many of the qualities of universe are “fine-tuned”.
Change one constant of the universe just the tiniest amount and the universe would
never exist. With matter, atoms, stars, and planets, there are a lot of “coincidences” that

need to line up to just create the basic universe we live in, with odds of this happening,
in ranges of like 1 in 10^500. That is a number vastly bigger than all the atoms in
universe times the number of atoms in the universe. A common theist would look at
that, and say, yep, God created the universe, and their reason would be so wrong.
Science was right to question a God, and to find some way this could be possible. How
can the universe be fine-tuned to the most utmost level, and it be possible that this was
not done by a God creator?

Our own universe is already quite big, it is probably trillions of times larger or more,
than the universe we can even see. We will never see nor travel to any of it. A basic idea
is that there are many universes like our own super massive one, that sprang into
existence at the same time, and that every possible initial configuration of the universe
happened at once. You don’t need fine tuning if every possible option for that tuning,
happened, and we just happen to live in the one that worked. This is the basic idea of a
multi-verse, a reason why we need to have more than one universe, with different
physical properties than our own. This idea of multiverse is often made into absurd ideas
of alternate realities, time travel, and other dimensions. There is nothing magical, nor
that amazing about a multiverse, it is actually a bit boring an idea, that is little different
than there being more galaxies in our universe, than our own. These other universes
spread out from each other by great distances. They can just be really far away, beyond
any scale of imagining. It is almost another dimension of the universe would need to
create to describe that distance and not our normal 3D space dimensions in our own.

If you could leap far enough in any direction instantaneously, at a certain “distance”,
our whole universe we live in, would be like a distant star fading away, at a single point
of light, and bit farther, absolute darkness and nothing, and bit farther, another universe
coming like a small point of light, and we could go enter that universe, and its laws

would be different, though since it is right next door, it would probably be
indistinguishable from our own. To actually get to a universe with laws even different
than ours would require traveling many whole universes and the distances in between.
This is far, and basically so absurd to be nonsense. There is no way to test such a thing.
No way to experience any aspect of this, and no possible useful technology to make from
it. The more interesting thing we can investigate is how a universe comes into being.
Understanding how reality itself forms, and understanding that other universes can exist,
can free us to create reality very differently.

Now my idea of “distance” may be very wrong, and very hard to define, because we can
never escape our universe, nor even the tiny part of it we are in. the multiverse in this
simple explanation, is not what physics believes might be possible. It is just one aspect
of the idea.

Unified Field Theory/A Theory of Everything

General Relativity (GR) explains how space and time, are shaped, in such a way to
explain gravity. Gravity is able to act on things at a distance with no particle or thing
moving between them. Einstein explained this, “spooky action at a distance” by changing
how we define the geometry of space and time. Gravity curves space and time, and that
curvature changes what a straight line is from our perception of it. There are many ideas
in GR that are deeply cherished in physics, and changing any one of them is a big deal.
GR is a deterministic model. At its heart, it is still Newtonian (classical).

Gravity is a description of time, and how things point towards the future. Things with
more time, experience more time, and thus are slower moving in time. Objects then

orient towards things with more time, and point towards them, and eventually become
entangled in that things time frame. The future can be a literal direction a thing is
pointed towards and moving towards. This movement and change has to be described
with changes in time, rather than just pure motion. At extremes of lots of time and little
time, very unique and unintuitive things happen, relative to movement on Earth. We live
in the time frame of the earth, and it takes a lot of energy for us to change our future
away from it. To travel to another star is to fundamental change one’s time frame from
their home stars. Seeing gravity as a direction time is pointing, and that its force is
driven by changes in geometry that can only be seen with “clocks”, is odd. When we go
to the tiniest level, the entire way to understand gravity completely changes. It becomes
nearly impossible to describe with discrete and indivisible objects.

Quantum Physics, is a way to explain how things work at the tiniest levels, the quantum
level. We can’t directly observe quantum physics, in the same way we can observe the
motion of stars and galaxies. The way matter works at the smallest level is completely
contrary to how it works at large scales. Quantum physics is defined by quantum
uncertainty. It explains this with probability wave functions. Matter is a set of
probabilities understood by the mathematics of waves. The math to explain quantum
physics is done with statistics. It works nearly perfectly with empirical observation, and
yet defies any intuitive way of understanding it. Things both exist and don’t exist, at the
same time. The universe is purely random, at the quantum level, according to the math
that explains it and the empirical observations made of it. It is non-deterministic. True
randomness and not chaos rules. Physics though likes to explain it all in nice ordered
deterministic ways, and this creates tremendous conflict among physicists. The current
models of physics always strive to push the random non-determinism of quantum
physics into determined models, no matter how wild the idea has to be to do it.

These two very contradictory theories of GR and Quantum Mechanics are equally good at
describing their scales of the universe. To bring these two ideas into a singular idea
requires 2 possible routes, use quantum theory to explain GR, or use GR to explain
quantum theory. At a philosophical level there are two possibilities, 1. Build a
deterministic model that explains quantum uncertainty, or 2. Build a non-deterministic
(probability) model, that can make a deterministic like system. Physics has basically two
theories to do this, “Many Worlds” (determinism is right) and the “Multiverse” (nondeterminism is right). It is for me, just in my opinion, a difference between a world from
everything, a singularity, or a universe from nothing, the ground state.

The Multiverse/Megaverse:

The universe we live in is vastly larger than the one we can see. If you took every atom
in the knowable universe and made that into an entire independent, universe, that would
still be a very small size. The universe is determined by the initial conditions of the
universe, where the laws and the constants of the universe are determined for the life
the universe. Currently we describe this with differing big bang theories, in the study of
Cosmology. Our universe has many constants, that if changed even the slightest bit, the
universe wouldn’t exist. The likelihood of this happening by chance is very slim. Stable
evolving universes like ours are very rare, with all the possible conditions a universe
could have. Most all the universes out there, are just duds, where nothing really
happened.

The multiverse is an attempt to explain a fine-tuned universe, with no creator. How we
can have this perfectly made and balanced universe, and have no god that created it. In
order for this very rare set of initial conditions to have happened, there must have been
many universes. All possible initial conditions happened, and we just happen to be in the

one that allowed for life. 10^500 is a number that get put around for the number of
universes that could be in a multiverse. Basically, if you try enough times, crazy rare
things can happen. It is not an infinitely big multiverse; its massive size can only be
understood in statistics and not in quantity of space to conceive of existing. It is best to
imagine the multiverse as colorful images and dream like fantasies of statistics rather
than try to “see” the actual universe.

“Parallel” worlds, are not something we can just jump into, any more than travel 1
trillion light years, in 1 second. They are far away. The “Mega-Verse” is a better word for
it than the multiverse, because it describes a truly massive universe, with many massive
universes. These universes, all exist at the same time, for a basic form of the theory,
and are separated by great distances from each other. In a sense our already large
universe, which might be trillions of times bigger than we can see, is then multiplied by
10^500 possible universes. I personally think of this is in a chromatic way. Sort of like a
circle rainbow, and our universe is a tiny sliver or even photon in the spectrum of a
circular rainbow. And every photon in that rainbow is its own universe, with a slightly
different color and wavelength. Photons close to each other would be nearly identical. All
the universes “near” us, would probably be indistinguishable from this one, if they all
began at the same moment. A chromatic rainbow multi-verse, with color defining each
universe unique tuning of its starting properties, makes sense to my imagination.
Physics often uses color as analogy to explain quantum theories, so a made-up name
like, Quantum Chromatic Cosmology (QCC), wouldn’t sound that weird, in physics.

Sequential Multiverse (Time and Space)

Universes could be born out of other universes. In this model, a “multiverse” is
separated by lengths in time, and not just distance. You have to travel in time to go into

another universe, rather travel across distances to reach another universe. We can have
a multiverse divided by distances in time and/or space. A more developed version of the
multiverse also evolves in time, if you go forward in time, you can enter another
universe, that arises out of this one. My work in this book will be about how a universe
evolves into another universe through time. The multiverse only concerns itself with the
initial conditions of the universe. I will explore how to build universes from nothing, that
evolve into other universes. We can talk about what happens before the big bang
intelligibly, even though, all time we experience begins at that moment, because of how
space and time can flip their relationship to each other in white or black holes.

Many Worlds Interpretation (MWI):

A Many-Worlds-Interpretation (MWI) model of the universe can explain a lot and it is a
very consistent model. It is a difficult model to fully accept with the existence of freewill. Quantum theory uses a completely probabilistic model to determine quantum
states, no quantum state can exactly be known, ever under any conditions, and can only
use probability to determine it. It is spinning up with a “½” chance, it is spinning down
with a “½” chance (1 over the square root of 2, if you get basic trig, and use the
Pythagorean-theorem). This is the reality of the quantum world.
o

Uncertainty principle and Schrodinger’s/Dirac’s equations.

o

We describe particles positions, with probability waves

o

We can describe things as being in 2 possible states at the same time.
With different probabilities for those states being actually material real.

Physicists are very divided by this, and think of this probability as more of a math trick,
and that we don’t understand the real underlying conditions. One solution is to make
every possible state that a quantum state can be in, to be contained in its own universe.
Every possible state that a quantum particle can occupy as described by a quantum

probability wave, is its own universe. Every particle in the universe, would have a
universe for every single state it could be in, for its whole life. 10^500 particles, time
10^500 states, with 10^500 universes, makes for a lot of universes.

We can imagine our universe as like a sheet of paper, and we are just experiencing a
line being drawn through that, except that the piece of paper would be like 4-10
dimensions instead of 2 like a flat piece of paper. (take your time to wrap your head
around this). if you were to follow a line, that would be one universe. Though you could
in theory just draw a line anyway you wanted, and each drawing of a line would be a
valid universe. All the different dimensions are just different ways that things can move,
the different possibilities. A simple 3-d block just wouldn’t be able to contain the
possibilities, that quantum states could be in. We are just a pencil line drawn across a
10-dimensional flat piece of paper. The line would be time itself, the direction our
universe took through this super universe. The overall 10-dimensional block is just a
singular thing, where everything that could ever happen, happened. A sheet of paper (a
vector space) has Infinite lines with every possibility the universe could take in its entire
life, existing. This also assumes a deterministic universe, with no free will, no freedom,
and completely meaningless universe.

The main idea is hard to understand. If there is randomness in quantum physics, the
only way to make it determined is to say that all those possibilities something can exist
in, exist, and are real, and we just live in a simpler universe where we describe them as
probabilities. This is a bit like the allegory of the cave, and there being a higher
dimensional world that we only see as simpler dimensional representations of on a cave
wall. For MWI, even outside the cave is its own illusion, and a casting on the wall of a
higher more real dimensions. Our freedom is an illusion created from a perfect world we

can never exist in or experience directly. This idea is a very powerful one for a creating a
strong scientific model that can account for “truth” without probability.

Big Bangs and My Argument on White Hole Cosmology

The universe doesn’t have to begin in a singularity, and there is no scientific evidence
nor working math for that, in physics now. The big bang theory is not a theory that the
universe began in a singularity, all the evidence sort of proved that wrong. What we call
the beginning of the universe in the big bang theory, is the exact moment after what is
called “inflation”. At 10^-32 seconds is the moment inflation ended, and the moment
physics has no idea what happened before it. They assume it was a singularity, and thus
use the word “inflation” to describe it. Well if existence didn’t begin at the big bang, and
the universe we live in came out of another universe, then a single point of super
condensed energy is a very unlikely starting state for a universe. The universe beginning
from a region of massively expanded space is more likely. This size would be like that of
the size of our observable universe at the moment “inflation” “ended”. This would of
course be an area much larger than we could ever see in theory, because our universe is
much larger than what we can ever see, unless we are the exact center of all reality and
are the universe. This is so unlikely to the point of being impossible.

Our universe most likely begins in a region of massively expanded empty space, like that
described by the size of space caused by cosmic inflation, though many times bigger,
depending how much bigger our little universe is compared to what we can see. An
interesting fact about the universe is that the net energy in it is zero, there is equal
amounts of negative energy, as there is to positive energy. Gravity has negative energy.
So, the universe comes from nothing, and nets out in everything, to be nothing. Time
then seems to have negative energy.

Chapter 12: Space And Time

Origins of The Universe: Structure of A Big Bang Singularity

I presume the universe begins from nothingness, from purely random forces of
probability. The universe at its very root and origin is utterly and completely random
without form, meaning, or structure. True nothingness is the “thing” that preexists time,
and is the minimal non-material/non-tangible thing, that anything could come from. If
probability defines energy, then energy existed in the nothingness before existence, at
least the potential for it. It was energy without order, structure, causality, or direction.
Energy itself was and is just pure random probabilities in nothingness being expressed.
Higher energy things are less likely than lower energy things, and this instability in
probability makes them more likely to decay to more probable lower energy states. This
correlation can be so high as to be the basis of describing energy itself. Matter is a stable
form of low probability fields that don’t decay into higher probability low energy fields.

Energy of some form most likely existed before time itself developed, such as how we
describe the big bang singularity as a massive ball of energy without time. It was all
potential and probable energy and no actual structure, form, causality or time. The
singularity of a big bang is itself nearly infinitely small. It is something best described by
my 0D models of space, where all of reality is a single non-determined point. The
universe comes from a space of nearly infinite smallness. Imagining true nothing
nothingness is a hard-mental challenge. Empty space is still something, it can be
measured and you can have more or less of it, in mostly exact amounts. True
nothingness is like zooming in on any point in the universe and you keep zooming in as
far as you can go and never stop zooming. You enter a space of the infinitely small. You

begin to relate to minimal scales the universe forms from, that we can’t observe yet,
with science.

Space is something. This is truly nothing. Only the possibility of something exists. In
nothingness, there is still “something”. Timelessness doesn’t mean eventlessness.
Moments/events come into being from chance, and then die. A singularity of
nothingness, can form into anything, and just end. If you imagined our universe having
a big bang, then a big crunch, with nothing happening in our universe effecting the next
universe, this has a certain timeless quality when you step back and look at all the
universes coming and going out of being between big bangs and “big crunches”. There is
no way to order a sequence of which one came first and which one went after. There is
no chain of causality in any form. The random fluctuations in a big bang singularity are
equal to the birth and death of a whole universe, without time, so nearly infinite ones
can happen and there is no means to define them in sequence. You could just say that
all the universes that came and went, all happened at the same time, or in sequence in
any order, and it wouldn’t matter.

This space where the universe ceases to exist as a thing bound in time, is timeless, and
yet is full of energy, possibility and “events”. This is a timeless, highly active,
nothingness. Just randomness popping in and out of existence, with no real past or
future. One event doesn’t affect the next event. The random structure has no real form
or consistency that can have time, nothing causes something else to happen, nothing
can evolve and develop into something else. In theory, anything could pop into
existence in this nothingness 0D universe. Our whole universe as it is now, could pop
into existence, with nothing happening before it. The more complex the structure, the
more unlikely for it to possibly happen in a given moment, from one moment to the
next. The big bang could have just formed into the exact universe we see before us, with

us as we are exactly now, with nothing happening before that. The only way to disprove
such a reality is probability. It is possible, and it is also the least likely of all possible
things to explain our existence. Finding a model that uses the simplest and most likely
configurations of the initial universe is a key problem in physics. There are a lot more
simpler systems than there are complex systems, and the universe we have most likely
evolved from a sort of rare and special simple system.

Maybe trillions upon trillions of “universes” popped out of nothing, and just died in the
next moment, one after the other. In a void of nothing, a possibility exists for something
to happen. Something happens, and then it ends, the following universe will have no
relationship to the one before. There will be no enduring structure. A universe would not
have time, nor size, of any meaning in our imagination. Pure nothing, creating
meaningless somethings, and back to nothing. Endless moments of near existence, or
just nothing. The singularity doesn’t need to have all the energy we see in the universe
contained in a single point. It just needs the possibility to randomly form into a structure
that endures and evolves into the one we have now. A very simple universe much
different than our own could have preceded the sort of high complexity universe we see
today. Something like the vacuum/space is the most likely thing to pop into random
existence out of nothing. The most minimal thing in this universe that can exist and
grow, would be the most likely thing to first exist.

Dark Energy, Expanding Space, And Entropy

The vacuum is the least possible thing that exists and is the most likely thing to have
been created at random from nothing. The vacuum has the minimum possible energy
anything can possess in the universe, and has the least of anything, that a thing can
have. Our, normal, very conception of nothing is the vacuum. Nothing is really nothing.

And in nothing random things can happen, because all things are possible. A bunny can
just appear from nothing, fully formed, and be the whole of the universe, as a
possibility, and this is standard physics. It is also good physics. It is the most likely way
to create life, according to probability (Boltzmann Brain). Impossible things don’t
happen. Very improbable things can happen and do happen. The most direct way for the
universe to have a sentient brain, is for it to just randomly appear out of nothing, in a
large enough universe that has existed over a long enough time. I called this a
“Heisenberg Apple” in an earlier chapter, to describe any object just coming into being
from nothingness, and yet in any empty space there is some probability of the possible
existence of any possible and real thing emerging in that space, thus making there never
be a zero quantity of anything in a set piece of space able to contain possible things. The
simplest way to get to absolute intelligence is for it to just appear and not evolve, and
this has the lowest statistical possible chance of being the way sentience and a god like
brain emerges. Any other solution requires complex ideas, and this part of the book will
try to show a way to get there. The vacuum is the most likely thing to appear from
empty space because it is the simplest stable structure in the universe, and thus it
makes a good basis to propose how to build a sentient being from nothing.

The very first thing was space, the vacuum; Its very first quality is that it got more
complex over time. The simplest possible universe, is the most likely universe to
randomly pop into existence out of nothingness. Time itself is measured by the
expansion of space, by the amount the vacuum has expanded. This is because in order
for something to exist it must influence the thing after it, and if empty space is static
and doesn’t influence itself, it has no time. Entropy itself emerges from the decay of
vacuum space into more vacuum space. Universal expansion (dark energy), the
properties of the vacuum, time, entropy, are as highly correlated as things can be in
modern physics, and thus most likely all the same thing. Time could be an emergent

property of entropy, that itself is the growth of nothingness into something, where one
event influences the next event.

Boltzmann Boxes and Boltzmann Brains

This is an idea correlated to Boltzmann’s theory of entropy and how the universe began.
In a Boltzmann’s box, he idealized a simple idea of how the universe began. Imagine a
box with a bunch of particles on one side, all bundled up into a singularity. Over time
entropy will spread those particles through the box. He defines each particle as able to
randomly jump to any location in time, and gain increasing complexity through time.
This is like a stove emitting heat to fill a cold room. A single particle can jump across the
whole room; it is unlikely but possible. The particles can jump any distance, and with
closer distances being more likely. Like in a gas, there is a mixture of cooler and hotter
particles all mixed together, and their average temp is what we call the temperature of a
gas. There are actually very hot and cold atoms mixed together, and the hotter ones
have higher probabilities of jumping larger distances randomly. Particles begin all
bundled up, and can randomly move in time. Probability will allow those particles to form
into complex structures, because they in theory can just jump into any configuration.
One of those structures will form a stability and cause a stable pattern to emerge out of
the random chaos. Swirls can move and bounce around in the box, and arise from pure
random distribution of particles. Entropy of particles can actually describe a big bang and
it forming those particles into the galactic like structures we see today, if certain weird
special patterns emerge from randomness. These simple yet impactful patterns that
cause new events to happen after them, and lead step by step to more structure in
system. A simple pattern, that isn’t that unlikely to happen, that can create something
after itself and evolve into more and more.

I take basic Boltzmann entropy as it explains cosmology, and add in one more feature.
Space is entropic. It isn’t just matter rearranging itself, it is also space rearranging itself.
It is growing, moving, shifting. In a Boltzmann Box of particles distributing randomly
through that box in time, space is also distributing itself. If you imagine a large box and
bunch or particles gathered at one end, and then let them go, they will distribute
themselves through the box. Space too is distributing itself and “moving”. So that space
is also expanding, always moving. A box itself expands from space expanding, and not
just particles hitting the wall. Space itself may be part of the dispersion of the particles,
where tiny amounts of space that can emerge probabilistically in a singularity drive it to
disperse through a room. Space is more fundamental than matter, it has energy, it has
entropy. It may also be the source of entropy in systems, where we observe matter
gaining entropy in time, it is in reality the underlying space that could be driving that
change.

Space itself is a quality of that box, and also randomly distributing itself and growing.
Boltzmann may have gotten what has entropy wrong in that system, or at least my
understanding of his work is wrong. The geometry of vacuum space will become
something fundamental to physics if my hypotheses in this chapter are true. I initially
saw the structure as big “hexagons” with tiny particles at their loci, all moving and
transforming. With later education and looking for better visuals, it seems more similar
to “Penrose Tiles”. The pattern of space as it relates to entropy and time, is probably a
well-defined structure in ancient eastern religious art, somewhere. The math is out there
and probably already well worked out, for something seemingly completely unrelated.

Space and The Vacuum as The Graviton

In current science the “curvature” of space, creates gravity, and not any sort of particle
emitting out from matter. They theorize about a possible particle called a “graviton” that
makes gravity possible, though have no way to even explain what it would do, or how to
observe it. Space itself might be that “particle” that they call the graviton. Gravity is able
to influence things at a distance with nothing exchanging in between. It is not like a ball
hitting a ball, and causing something to happen. This “Spooky action at a distance”, was
a nearly unsolvable puzzle. Newton could not solve it, and directly said that he left this
problem to future scientists to solve. Einstein solved this by explaining it as a curvature
of space-time altering an object and bringing it towards another object. This then begs
the question what is “curvature”, what is being “curved”, as this all relates to gravity and
space-time. Gravity has a high correlation to entropy, universal expansion, time, space,
and possibly entanglement. The fact that around matter there is more gravity, is a sort
of illusion, that confuses us as to what the real causality might be. The order in which we
discover things, is not their order in importance or causality.

Gravity can be seen as a description of how space moves, rather than just curves. The
exchange of force is not like being hit by an object with mass. You are hit with a particle
that is time itself; it’s very movement through things, creates time and the very shape
of space in the universe. Space itself is like a super “massive” particle, with no mass that
moves through anything. As “time” passes through things, it shifts that thing to one side
because space is unequal to the space on the other side due to differences in relative
time. Where space is shorter, it moves towards that direction. You can apply this same
idea towards time, as time moves slower, matter moves towards slower moving regions
of space time. The faster moving space time, that is more expanded pushes it towards
the slower moving less dense space region. space pointing away from it towards vast
amounts of space.

Space is not curved around a gravitational object. Space doesn’t have density. Denser
space is larger space, and is measured in size. If the sun was curving space to create
gravity, then the distance between the sun and the earth would be increasing. Time is
being shifted. If space is entangled and experiences entropy in that entangled structure,
then space has a direction that it moves in as it expands. The directionality and flow of
space creates what we call curvature, and the more it flows out from something, the
more things are attracted towards it. The direction that space moves in is time. Space
itself creates time, and is time. The structure of space has a pattern that grows and has
entropy, that entropy is like a form of “radiation”. The space-time field emits new space
as its “particle”.

ENTROPY IS QUANTUM GRAVITY

Space-time itself then has to imbed information about the universe in its own structure.
At the tiniest levels, space-time can be micro-curved, and those curves can contain
information that can influence the universe around it. There are different ways to look at
a solution to this and they are all probably roughly equal, eventually. You can create
what is called “gravitational waves”, and describe them as oscillations at very tiny levels.
These waves on larger scales exist, and our scientific instruments to detect them, can
only work on the largest possible waves, at this time in history. The waves created in
pure space time, can in of themselves have energy, mass, and information imbedded in
them. When we consider the entropy of a system, we can also consider that there are
micro gravitational waves emitting out from it containing the information of that system.
That we observe particles bouncing around, but in reality, the heat we observe coming
off of something, also contains its information in space time itself. The way heat moves
could be a product of gravity operating on the quantum scale. Entropy is quantum

gravity, and a proper theory of entropy has to explain how it warps time and space at
the smallest levels.

Time itself is a kind of “particle” that is not matter. It is better described as a pattern, a
replicating system, operating on the tiniest scales of reality. It is itself defined by what
the tiniest scale of reality can be, since time is the very “pixels” from which reality is
created. This is taken Einstein’s General Relativity, literally and not figuratively like many
physicists do. In GR gravity is not a force, and is just how space and time move relative
to material objects. Gravity is space-time and inertia according to Einstein’s work. If we
want to apply this to the smallest scales, then we just need describe how systems
change at the smallest, scales, in time and space, and then say this pattern creates what
we see at the largest scales. The specific math of GR doesn’t apply to the small, it
applies to the big. It is the general math, ideas and axioms that do apply. Geometry is
king.

All the problems found in the study of black-holes and information lost is solved by this
shift in thinking, and with the way I described space time in special relativity. We just
have to learn to imagine dimensionality and space itself better, so we can see these
ideas. All the information in a black-hole is embedded in space-time. That information
can cross the event horizon of a black hole, with enough time, because space-time can
be “emitted” from a black-hole. The interior of the black-hole and its singularity will
contain the structure of space-time at the smallest and most discrete levels on massive
scales. A singularity from the inside is massive walls and not a singular point. Seeing a
black hole like this is simply a simple literal description of GR.

A Toy Universe

Imagine “a universe”, it is singular, and not the one we live in. It had a “big bang” and it
will have an end. This universe has a finite life. It is born and it will die. The unique
quality of this universe is that the end state of the universe will affect the beginning
state of the universe that comes after it. So, this imagined “universe” begins, and this
“universe” ends. In sequence, with the conditions of the preceding universe affecting the
following universe. It will be the same as the previous one, or adopt a minor change that
can add more stability and “longer life” to the universe. In a sequential evolving
universe, you need a first universe. Each universe that comes after the one before, will
evolve on top of the one before it. The universe arose out of nothing, and due to pure
chance and pure probability. Simple order can evolve into larger and more complex
systems, that can perpetuate themselves forward.

The whole of a theoretical universe that could evolve and pass its order on, could be as
small as say 2 photons. The next universe after it would be 2 photons again, rather than
just random. Two entangled photons, spreading out for a trillion years, until that
entanglement breaks, and the energy of that resets the universe. The conditions of this
next universe would not be purely random; they would arise out the history and end
state of that universe of two entangled photons. This universe after many cycles could
have a small change that actually works and makes the universe little “better”, and it
transfers this improvement into the next universe. More entangled photons, would make
more universes to grow. If the photons could replicate, then there could be a lot more
universe, and lot more opportunities for change.

In a more realistic universe, at one moment, in an empty universe, with no net positive
energy, a possibility happened. The smallest possible thing happened. All the random
fluctuations created something. This was the smallest possible thing that could exist, and

not a massive singularity. Something more than nothing came into existence. This had
happened for nearly infinite times before. On this day, the first day came into existence.
It was the tiniest thing, and the tiniest thing that could be and keep existing.

If you do something enough times, some very odd possibilities will happen. This was not
a monkey typing the complete works of Shakespeare unlikely. In physics, there is a
definitive possibility that the whole universe could just appear as a fully functioning
bunny rabbit. It could just appear out of nothing, as a pure possibility. If the universe
was created by pure chance in a one-shot deal, with all possible universes being made,
then a big bunny rabbit is the most likely universe to come into existence. In physics,
they call this a Boltzmann’s Brain, I prefer a Big Bunny Rabbit (BBR). The most likely
thing to happen is the most absurd one, if all we had was one chance at intelligence in
the universe, it would just be a wholly sentient super god brain, that was all things. This
though is too unlikely. Something far more likely happened than this, because it was far
more likely. The most likely thing that could happen, is that the universe had its very
first stable state. It didn’t just come and go. It endured a bit. It had some sort of
structure. A little bit of vacuum space coming into being, or a BBR, have absolutely
different probabilities of having happened. This tiny little state, would have special
properties.

ENTANGLEMENT SPACE-TIME GEOMETRY

Quantum entanglement is one of the newest discovery and it is very weird, and it can be
the basis and fundamental causality for all creation. Instead of being something we
attach on to theories we use to describe the universe, it probably should lie at the
foundational root of all theories, and be the primary/first thing we study, even as
children. At a quantum level it is structure creating, and has odd properties that are very

difficult to explain when applied to particles. If it was the space beneath particles that
was entangled, it might make a theory of entanglement more intuitively accessible, with
the right visuals.

The universe before time was endless random events with no connection between the
one before it. It was a universe that could be anything at any moment, just flashing into
probable configurations. The simple ones would be more common, with complex ones
rare. Like a monkey typing out Shakespeare, is nearly impossible. Three words of
Shakespeare written at random by a monkey on a typewriter is much more likely, than a
whole play. Our universe forming is more like all the poets in history being typed in the
order they wrote, by 1 single monkey. It is possible, though the more likely is just a
simple sequence that can eventually evolve into the universe now, step by step. The
very beginning and end of universes could be as trivial as virtual particles appearing and

you know where a left arrow is exactly. This entanglement can just be directionality. A

The 3 Proposed Axioms

Axiom 1: Evolution of Space-Time

•

Axiom 1: A state has time when it can define the states that follow it. States that
don’t influence the following states, don’t have time.

•

Abstract version 1: The initial state of a “universe” can be influenced by the
preceding “universe”.

•

Abstract version 2: The initial states of the universe evolve into more stable
forms, from the events in the preceding universe into the next one.

This is not a very controversial idea for an axiom if you accept the idea, that universes
are born out of universes. This can only be reached as an idea when there are no other
ways to explain the universe. An axiom like this, could be developed out in an empirical
analysis of vacuum states, and making theoretical models how a stable structure could
form and last in it. If one piece of entangled space is going “left”, you know its entangled
pair is going “right”.

In the real world, “virtual particles” forming in the vacuum of space, are just popping in,
popping out, with no net energy being made or destroyed. A photon has a probability to
appear, it appears sometimes, and then just disappears. It is not stable. It can’t build on
itself, or exist in time for longer than a single moment. If we can have virtual particles as
real things, then we can have odd things happen once in the life a universe, where
virtual particles can into something, that just doesn’t disappear, in the next moment.
Stephen Hawking built an entire career on making virtual particles into stable entities, in
a narrow use case. If two entangled virtual particles formed at the event horizon a black
hole and one fell through and the other didn’t, this would form electromagnetic radiation,
that would glow off a black hole, a sort of super minimum heat, that an object could
shine off. This “Hawking radiation”, is the “coldest”/lowest energy light in the universe,
and there is no way to observe it. this light though is a simple theoretical stable
structure, that persists in existing, rather than just pops in out of existence like a virtual
particle. These two entangled virtual particles take very different paths in time, and
become fundamentally divided from each other. One went into a black hole, and the
other didn’t. This breaking of symmetry creates energy that can be seen as a photon.
Light is created from nothing, in Hawking’s of model of a black hole. Or in my
perspective, light is created from information, found in entropy, that is defined by
geometries in space-time, which is “nothing”/empty space, in our real world.

Within those many but small chances, there are these very special rare possibilities, very
rare, very small in change, and that build onto the thing that comes before it. In life,
mutations that actually produce something useful and completely new are extremely
rare. When they do happen, and those mutations don’t make a living thing infertile, it
can pass those changes on to the next generation, forever. Life on earth, shares mostly
the same DNA and mostly all the same biological systems. Even bugs have hearts and
blood and the same basic chemistry as us. While we see a great deal of variety of life on
earth, it is in reality fairly homogenous, and sharing the majority aspects across different
classes of life forms. Tiny variations in the functional forms of life creates all the variety
of life we see on earth. Humans and natural watermelons are not that different. Humans
and domesticated watermelons are more similar at a memetic level. Evolution itself is
just a how genetic information moves, and evolves from simple systems to complex
systems. All “real” information evolves and grows, and I just take evolutionary
information theory, memes, and push it backwards into the origin of universes. We can
treat whole universes as an individual “animal”, for this argument.

In a theoretical universe, a “trait” gets passed on to the next universe. These traits are
part of how a universe evolves and grows, and the mutation itself is creating the next
universe, and this is why that mutation can persist into the next universe. Successful
mutations are those that survive more, that are “stronger”, that “create” more universe,
and that add stability for the universe to exist more. In universes giving birth to new
universes, stability and being-as-simple-as-possible are the most likely thing to happen,
and thus what does happen. The universe which makes more universes, which adds to
the growth, and adds to the stability, such that more things become possible, while the
universe also doesn’t rip itself apart, is the one that will survive. Any universe that is
even 1% less productive, will over time, fade into nothing compared to more successful
universe.

The universe moves in two directions, outwards with space and time as it expands, and
inwards towards its initial ground state. Entropy adds complexity to the system, and

systems, that creates an expansion of entangled space-time structures. Things go to

nearly infinite dimensions and can be any number. It goes with more likely things, more
simple things, and only possible things. The ground state is everywhere.

Axiom 2: The Consistency of Time

Axiom of Time: The speed of causality is consistent across all possible
universes

Space should be viewed like a particle, in some aspects. It can pass through anything. It
has an orientation and a directionality in its movement. The directionality of space’s
movement, is where time itself emerges from. Space passing through things, creates a
directionality in time, an experience in time. So as space expands out from a planet or
sun, it slows time opposite the direction it flows towards. This dilation causes
gravitational attractive forces
•

Time is space with a direction

•

That direction is created from the entropy of entanglement

•

Entangled space has only direction as a property

Time has a structured and ordered sequence across all universes, because that is the
requirement for time to even exist, if it didn’t there wouldn’t be causality and without
causality, there would be no time. You can never personally experience any other speed
of time, different than the one you occupy. All experience time as absolute relative to
themselves in the same way. If you were placed in different regions of space time with
time traveling at different rates, you would experience time exactly the same. It is
impossible to directly experience time as anything different than your own experience of
it, regardless of any concepts of consciousness. Clocks don’t feel time dilation. A second
is second, in your own time frame. You can never experience time move at a different
rate, you can’t experience time in slow or fast motion, as anything more than your brain
processing things differently. Even if between every second whole universes were born
and died, a second would just pass.

Imagine we had a massive multiverse, the only thing that would preserve the stability
and separation of universes is the inability to cross over into the other. There needs to
be an inherent separation of universes. If the speed of causality wasn’t constant, there
couldn’t be one universe after the other. The previous universe could just jump into the
next if separated by time, or jump over to the next, if separated by distance. Or in in our
own universe, all the light of every star we could possibly see could just bombard us at
once.

You can measure the time of the universe by its expansion, in absolute terms. A person
by a black hole’s event horizon, will experience a slower rate of time, than a person a
few kilometers away. Certain galaxies distances from each other is an absolute clock for
the universe, no matter where you are observing them, so long as they are truly distant

from you. This distance between galaxies will be a “clock” for the universe. The person
near a black hole event horizon, where time travels slower, will see this happen faster.
There can be a measure of “simultaneous” events determinable by the relationship each
observer has of this separation. Though they will observe each galaxy differently. A
person near an event horizon seeing the universe passing buy faster than any other
possible place in the universe, would also be bombarded with all the light from a large
amount of time, in a short time. Where one might even feel the heat of a distant star,
like the way we feel the sun.

The consistency of time is the consistency of the universe as a real thing. We may all see
time differently and yet can all understand each other’s different time frames in absolute
terms. If you have 2 different time frames viewing the same thing, the sort of
information you would need to transform your observation of an event, into the
perceived observation of another’s event, would describe your theory of time. Observer
A sees one thing and Observer B sees another. This can be described a set of
information for each observer. The information will look different. The sort of rule or set
of information can I use to transform one set of information into other set of
information, observing the same this, is a theory of time. If there is no rule nor way to
do this, then time is not consistent, and is based solely on how it is observed in that
moment, and with no relation to anything else. This is just my very poor way of
understanding Einstein’s conflict with Niels Bohr about reality and “God not playing dice
with the universe”.

If time is just the size the of the universe, then that size can be consistent, even across
universes. This would be possible if universes are created from the space-time of a
previous universe. And if information from a previous universe could be contained in the
space time of a previous universe, then universes could create universes and pass on
information between them, to create one from the other. Time being consistent across

all universes can be translated into a statement about all of reality being one megaverse definable by one consistent set of information/“number”. The big bang can’t be a
wholly strict separation from other universes in a possible multi-verse, nor the soul
beginning of time.

Axiom 3: The Probability of the Possible and Impossible

Axiom 2: The only things that can exist are what are possible to exist.

My Probability Rule: The least likely things to happen are the most likely things
to happen, because there are a lot more unlikely things, then there are likely
things.

Determinism arises out a fundamental feature of probability, that which is possible, and
that which is impossible. Space time must be defined by probability and quantum
phenomena, and not some clockwork universe model of stiff materialism. A deterministic
model has practical use in its math and ease of use. In some ways determinism is
merely seeing the absolute universe beginning from its end. What is possible, and most
probable is a very narrow and very fine path, that leads to the universe we see before
us, and the amazing “created” universe we see. Physics and logic may love to believe
the universe is all determined, and yet we as humans know from the act of thinking that
the universe is not determined. Reality is clearly non-deterministic. On its largest scales
it is very deterministic, and on its smaller scales more random. Human thought is far
more connected to the smallest scales and how quantum information is processed,
rather than how stars move across the heavens or cannonballs fire from a cannon.

-The universe begins in pure probability. For something to exist is an act of
probability. For this probability to be known beforehand, would eliminate the
probability, and thus eliminate its existence.-

Complexity can be built out of chain of very small and very unlikely things, stacking on
top of each-other. A simple stable structure could form, then over time a rare event can
form another tiny change that adds more stability and structure. This can go on and on,
until the universe we live, comes to exist. Lots of small unlikely things aligning over
enough time, rather than just one huge creation of everything in one moment, is the
most likely way thing came into existence.

We can think of biology’s survival of the fittest applying to the tiniest aspects of the
universes laws, and they evolved into the ones we have. The evolution of life and all its
laws and logic, can themselves be emergent properties of how the universe and its laws
evolved from the tiniest details in step by step fashion with the tiniest of mutations,
where only a few out of near countless amounts would ever even work. Life is a natural
expression of the creation of the universe, from its very start.

A step towards more stability is very unlikely and very rare. When it does happen, it
becomes part of the “identity” of existence, and the next universe will develop with that
new very unlikely state, and not have to “learn” it again out of pure random chance.

If there was a moment where all possible starting states of the universe all began at
once, there wouldn’t be many that lasted. And our universe would probably look like
most of those that did last. Though this is an event too unlikely to happen and not
necessary to create the sheer complexity we see. We don’t need 10^500 universes
popping into existence at once. We only need 10^200-300 popping up randomly to get
to one single configuration that can evolve into the more complex one we have now. This
difference in odds is so large that only simple evolving systems would be likely possible
to create the universe, by 200-300 sigma (0’s). Evolution from simple to complex, step
by step, with lots of trial and error, in sequence, is far more likely. I doubt in all of
creation, in all universes that ever existed, fully formed sentient beings formed out of
nothing, even if it is possible, because the mega-verse isn’t old enough/big enough.

The universe had to evolve from state to state, and have almost no direction or purpose.
It just became a bit more stable, and all times absolutely consistent with what is
possible, within probability and the minimal basic states of the universe. Complexity had
to develop from simple to more complex, step by step, it couldn’t just leap, it was very
unlikely. The most likely thing is just a very small change, not BBRs appearing from
nothing.

What is possible and not possible, is probably the most important idea in all of
creation.

This simple idea seems to be a simple truism, it is however giving directionality to
creation and time. It is a basic axiom, and a pretty minimal one at that. It is for me the
basis of what people see as god in creation. In evolutionary biology, there are not that
many configurations of life, that can actually live and reproduce something possibly
better than it. This creates a great constraint on what is possible, and the creation of

things that look designed, but are in reality created out of pure probability. It is very
unlikely that sentient space faring alien life, will be that much different from us as
human beings, simply because there might only be “one” route to even develop to that
stage of life.

The universe had to develop with the most unlikely steps, and not highly likely ones.
This is more probable. Likely things are very unlikely to happen. A chain of very unlikely
events can be the most likely thing if they form into a chain that adds increased stability,
and that are in a sense a very rare super unlikely thing, that which is possible. If you
have 900 1/1000 chances, and one 1/10 chance. It is more likely that you will
experience a 1/1000 thing than a 1/10 thing. These more unlikely things are more
common and thus the simpler and the more likely things. More common and unlikely
things are simpler, than rare more likely things. Small and frequent jumps of energy can
end up at a large energy state. Small energy bursts are much more likely to happen, and
thus the more likely cause of the universe. Lower energy events are more likely than
high energy events. Energy itself might just be a measure of contained probabilities.
Low energy things are more likely than high energy things. A sentient mind forming from
nothing is a very high energy event, that is the simplest way to get there, and very
unlikely. A low energy event is far more common and simple, where a simple
arrangement of information is the most likely starting point of a universe, by a very
large statistical amount.

CHAPTER SUMMARY

Quantum reality most likely created space and time, because things develop from
smaller to bigger, in general, with evolution. Time emerged from space-time geometry in

the very small, in nothingness. Absolutely nothing has qualities, and features, that are
independent of time and space. Very few qualities can exist independent of time.

GR is defined by Space time geometry
